اس کے برخلاف اگر سرکہ کے معینہ مٹکے پر ضلع ہوا ہے مثلاً عورت نے کہا کہ یہ سر کہ بدل ضلع میں دونگی پھر معلوم ہوا کہ وہ سر کہ نہیں بلکہ شراب ہے تو ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک عورت پر مقدار مہر واجب ہوگی اور صاحبین کے نزدیک اس کے مثل سر کہ واجب ہوگا جیسا کہ مہر کے سلسلہ میں باب المھر میں گزر چکا۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ عورت نے مال کا ذکر کیا حالانکہ وہ مال نہیں تھا پس عورت اپنے شو ہر کو دھوکا دینے والی ہوئی اور عقد کے ضمن میں دھوکا دینا ضمان کو واجب کرتا ہے اس وجہ سے عورت مسمی کی ضامن ہوگی ۔ اور اس کے برخلاف اگر مولیٰ نے اپنے غلام کو شراب کے عوض مکاتب بنایا یا آزاد کیا تو اس صورت میں غلام پر اپنی قیمت واجب ہوگی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مولی کی ملک غلام میں متقوم ہے چنانچہ اگر کسی نے غلام کو غصب کر لیا تو غاصب پر قیمت واجب ہوگی حاصل یہ کہ علام قیمت دار چیز ہے اور مولیٰ اپنی ملکیت کو مفت زائل کرنے پر راضی نہیں ہے اور غلام بدل یعنی شراب کو سپرد کرنے پر قادر نہیں اس لئے کہ مسلمان کے حق میں شراب غیر متقوم ہے اس وجہ سے مبدل یعنی غلام کی قیمت واجب ہوگی اور رہا ملک بضع حالت خروج میں سودہ غیر متقوم ہے۔ اور بخلاف النکاح سے نکاح اور ضلع کے درمیان فرق بیان کیا ہے چنانچہ اگر شراب پر نکاح کیا گیا تو نکاح صحیح اور مہرمثل واجب ہوگا اور اگر خلع کیا تو ضلع صحیح اور عورت پر کچھ واجب نہیں ہو گا وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ بضع حالت دخول میں متقوم ہے اور حالت خروج میں غیر متقوم اور بضع کے حالت خروج میں غیر متقوم اور حالت دخول میں متقوم ہونے میں بھید اور راز یہ ہے کہ ملک بضع شریف اور قدرومنزلت کی چیز ہے اس لئے کہ اس شرافت کو ظاہر کرنے کے لئے بغیر عوض اس کا مالک بننا مشروع ہوا اور رہا بضع سے شوہر کی ملک کا ساقط کرنا تو وہ فی نفسہ شریف ہے۔ لہذا اس وقت مال واجب کرنے کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں۔
In contrast, if khul' was made on a specific pot of vinegar, e.g., the woman said 'I will give this vinegar as the substitute for khul'' and then it turned out it was not vinegar but wine, then according to Abu Hanifa the woman owes the amount of mahr (dower), and according to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) she owes the like of vinegar, as passed in the chapter on mahr. The proof is that the woman mentioned property while it was not property, so she deceived her husband, and deception in the context of a contract necessitates liability, so she is guarantor of the specified thing. And in contrast, if a master made his slave a mukatab or freed him for wine, then in that case the slave owes his own price. The proof is that the master's ownership in the slave is valuable (muttaqawwim); thus if someone usurped the slave, the usurper would owe the price. The point is that the slave is a valuable thing and the master did not consent to destroy his ownership for free, and the slave is unable to hand over the substitution (wine) because wine is non-valuable for a Muslim, so the substitute (i.e., the slave's price) becomes due. As for ownership of the vulva (bud') in a state of removal, it is non-valuable. And in contrast to marriage, the difference between marriage and khul' is explained: if marriage is contracted for wine, the marriage is valid and mahr al-mithl is due; if khul' is done, the khul' is valid and the woman owes nothing. The reason for the difference is that the bud' during consummation is valuable, and during removal (khul') it is non-valuable. The secret why the bud' is non-valuable during removal and valuable during consummation is that ownership of the bud' is a noble and honorable thing, so to manifest its nobility, ownership of it without compensation is legislated. As for removing the husband's ownership of the bud', that is noble in itself, so there is no need to impose wealth at that time.
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage presents three exceptions to the rule that invalid consideration yields no liability. The first is a case of misrepresentation: if the woman offers a specific jar thinking it is vinegar but it is wine, she is considered a deceiver because she mentioned property. Abu Hanifa holds she owes mahr al-mithl; the Sahibayn hold she owes the value of vinegar. This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, and the text refers to the mahr chapter for details. The second exception: if a master frees or makes a mukatab contract with his slave for wine, the slave must pay his own price because the master's property in the slave is valuable (muttaqawwim) and he did not consent to lose it for free. The slave cannot hand over wine, so he must compensate with his value. The third exception contrasts marriage with khul': in marriage, the bud' is valuable at the time of consummation (muttaqawwim), so if wine is given as mahr, the marriage is valid and mahr al-mithl is due. In khul', the bud' is being removed (ghayr muttaqawwim), so no compensation is due. The underlying rationale is that acquiring ownership of the bud' (like in marriage) is a noble act and therefore requires a consideration to show its nobility, whereas removing ownership (like in khul') is itself noble and does not require additional wealth.

Key Terms
مہر مثل (mahr al-mithl): The standard dower for a woman of her status, used as a substitute when the specified mahr is invalid or not specified.
مکاتب (mukatab): A slave who has made a contract with his master to purchase his freedom by paying installments.
بضع (bud'): The vulva, used metaphorically for the right of sexual access in marriage. In fiqh, it is considered a valuable commodity in marriage but not in khul'.
متقوم (muttaqawwim): Legally valuable property that can be sold and compensated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Abu Hanifa says the husband gets nothing; Sahibayn say he gets the value of wine.
B) Abu Hanifa says the wife owes mahr al-mithl; Sahibayn say she owes the value of vinegar.
C) Abu Hanifa says the divorce is ba'in; Sahibayn say it is raj'i.
D) Abu Hanifa says the khul' is invalid; Sahibayn say it is valid.

Key Takeaway
Three exceptions show that invalid 'iwad does not automatically terminate liability; the nature of the exchanged right determines whether compensation is due.

The Hanafi Principle: Mahr and 'Iwad in Khul'
Fiqhi maxim linking mahr and khul' compensation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi maxim linking mahr and 'iwad in khul', explain its a fortiori proof, and identify cases where the reverse does not hold.

Core Idea
What serves as valid mahr is automatically valid as khul' compensation, but the opposite is not always required.

This lesson explores a key principle from al-Hidayah: any item permissible as mahr (dower) is also permissible as 'iwad (compensation) in a khul' divorce. The reasoning is based on a fortiori logic (qiyas awla). However, as we will see, the scope of 'iwad is broader, so some forms of compensation acceptable in khul' would not be valid as mahr. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying both marriage and divorce transactions in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle
State the maxim 'ما جاز أن يكون مهرا جاز أن يكون بدلا في الخلع' – whatever can be mahr can be substitute in khul'. Recognize that this is a general permissive rule accepted by the Hanafi school.
The maxim is a qa'idah fiqhiyyah that links two contracts: nikah and khul'.
2
Understand the a fortiori proof
The proof is that mahr is paid for a valuable subject (the bud' in marriage is muttaqawwim). What suffices for the more valuable must logically suffice for the less valuable (the bud' in khul' is ghayr muttaqawwim).
This is a qiyas awla (a fortiori analogy), which is stronger than ordinary qiyas.
3
Recognize the limitation
Note that the reverse is not always true. Items that can be 'iwad may not be valid as mahr. The example given is 1-9 dirhams: valid as 'iwad but not as mahr due to the minimum mahr requirement.
This limitation prevents a hasty generalization and shows the practical scope of the maxim.
4
Apply the principle to a scenario
Given an item offered as 'iwad, first check if it qualifies as mahr. If yes, it automatically qualifies as 'iwad. If not, do not reject it outright; check the conditions of 'iwad separately.
The maxim provides a sufficient condition for 'iwad, not a necessary one.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وما جازان يكون مهر اجازان يكون بدلافي الخلع لان ما يصلح عوضا للمتقوم أولى ان يصلح لغير المتقوم ترجمہ امام قدوری نے کہا کہ جو چیز مہر ہو سکتی ہے ( وہ بالا جماع ) خلع کا عوض ہو سکتی ہے اس وجہ سے کہ جو چیز قیمتی بضع کا عوض ہو سکتی ہے بدرجہ اولی غیر قیمتی کا عوض ہو سکتی ہے۔ تشریح اس عبارت میں مصنف ایک ضابطہ بیان فرما رہے ہیں وہ یہ کہ جو چیز عقد نکاح میں مہر بن سکتی ہے وہ بالا تفاق عقد ضلع میں بدل ضلع بن سکتی ہے دلیل یہ ہے کہ عقد نکاح کے وقت ملک بضع مقتوم ہے اور ضلع کے وقت غیر متقوم الہذا جو چیز بضع متقوم کا عوض بن سکتی ہے وہ بضع غیر متقوم کا عوض بدرجہ اولی ہوسکتی ہے۔ البتہ اس کا برعکس نہیں ہے، یعنی جو چیز خلع میں عوض ہو سکتی ہو وہ نکاح میں مہر بھی ہو سکے ضروری نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے کہ بعض چیزیں ایسی ہیں جو بدل خلع بن سکتی ہیں مگر ہر نہیں بن سکتی مثلاً ایک درہم سے نو در ہم تک بدل خلع تو ہوسکتا ہےمگر مہر نہیں ہوسکتا۔ اسی طرح اگر یہ
He said: Whatever is permissible to be mahr is permissible to be a substitute in khul', because that which is suitable as a substitute for the valuable is more suitable for the non-valuable. Translation: Imam al-Quduri said: Whatever can be mahr (by consensus) can be the substitute in khul', because that which can be a substitute for the valuable bud' can a fortiori be a substitute for the non-valuable one. Explanation: In this phrase the author states a principle: whatever can be mahr in the marriage contract can, by agreement, be the substitute in the contract of khul'. The proof is that at the time of marriage, ownership of the bud' is valuable (muttaqawwim), and at the time of khul' it is non-valuable. Therefore, that which can be a substitute for the valuable bud' can a fortiori be a substitute for the non-valuable bud'. However, the reverse is not true: whatever can be a substitute in khul' does not necessarily have to be valid as mahr in marriage. Because there are some things that can be a substitute in khul' but not mahr, for example, from one dirham to nine dirhams can be a substitute in khul' but cannot be mahr. Similarly, if...
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage presents a fundamental principle of Hanafi fiqh concerning khul' and marriage. Imam al-Quduri states that any item valid as mahr (dower) in a marriage contract is also valid as 'iwad (substitute) in a khul' contract, and this is by consensus. The reason is that in marriage, the bud' (vulva) is valuable (muttaqawwim) because the husband acquires ownership, so the substitute must be property. In khul', the bud' is being released from ownership, which is non-valuable, so the substitute requirement is lighter. Therefore, what is good for the heavier case (mahr) is a fortiori good for the lighter case (khul'). However, the converse is not always true. Some items are valid as 'iwad in khul' but not as mahr. The example given is an amount between one and nine dirhams; these can be a substitute in khul' but not as mahr because there is a minimum for mahr (ten dirhams in the Hanafi school). This principle is a maxim (qa'idah) that guides the permissible compensations in these two contracts.

Key Terms
مہر (mahr): The dower paid by the husband to the wife in a marriage contract.
عوض ('iwad): The compensation paid by the wife to the husband in a khul' transaction.
متقوم (muttaqawwim): Valuable property that is legally recognized as such; can be owned and transacted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the principle regarding what can be 'iwad in khul'?
A) Anything can be 'iwad even if it cannot be mahr.
B) Whatever can be mahr can be 'iwad, but the reverse is not always true.
C) Whatever can be 'iwad can be mahr, but not vice versa.
D) The same items can be both mahr and 'iwad without exception.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the set of permissible 'iwad in khul' is larger than the set of permissible mahr, so the maxim only works in one direction.

Wife Says 'Khula on What is in My Hand' – Nothing There
Ruling when wife offers unspecified hand contents as khula compensation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a wife offers khula with a general expression like 'ma fi yadi' and apply the principle of generality (amm) in khula compensation.

Core Idea
If the wife says 'khula on whatever is in my hand' and she has nothing, she owes nothing – generality of expression protects from liability.

In this lesson, we examine a concise ruling from the Hanafi tradition about khula. The wife says to her husband, 'Divorce me by khula on whatever is in my hand,' but she has nothing. The ruling clarifies that she does not owe any compensation because the word 'ma' (what) is general and does not specifically promise wealth. This protects her from being held liable for deceiving her husband.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
The wife initiates khula by offering an unspecified compensation: 'ma fi yadi' (whatever is in my hand).
Khula is a divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation to the husband.
2
Examine the offer's wording
The word 'ma' is a general (amm) term that can include both wealth and non-wealth. It does not specifically promise mal (property).
Hanafis interpret general words in contracts literally unless context specifies otherwise.
3
Apply the principle of taghrir
Since the wife did not specify wealth, she is not considered to have deceived (taghrir) the husband into accepting the khula.
Deception (taghrir) would have made her liable for the promised amount.
4
Determine the ruling
Because there was no deception and no specific mal promised, the wife owes nothing. The khula is valid without compensation.
The husband's acceptance is deemed to be without expectation of material return.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عورت نے مرد سے کہا جو کچھ میرے ہاتھ میں ہے اس پر خلع کرلے اور عورت کے ہاتھ میں کچھ نہیں تھا عورت پر کچھ بھی لازم نہیں ہوگا

فان قالت له خالعنى على مافى يدى فخالعها ولم يكن في يدها شي فلا شئ على لانها لم تغره بتسمية المال

ترجمہ پس اگر عورت نے اپنے شوہر سے کہا مجھ کو ضلع دیدے اس چیز پر جو کچھ میرے ہاتھ میں ہے۔ پھر شوہر نے عورت کو ضلع دید یا ، حالانکہ عورت کے ہاتھ میں کچھ نہ تھا توعورت پر کوئی چیز واجب نہیں ہوگی۔ کیونکہ عورت نے شوہر کو مال کا نام لے کر بھوکا نہیں دیا ہے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ ظاہر ہے اس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ عورت کے کلام مافی بدی میں لفظ ما عام ہے جو مال اور غیر مال سب کو شامل ہے اس وجہ سے عورت مال کا ذکر کر کے اپنے شوہر کو دھوکا دینے والی شمار نہیں ہوگی اور جب دھوکا دینے والی نہیں ہے تو کسی چیز کی ضامن بھی نہیں ہوگی۔
If a woman says to her husband: 'Divorce me by khula on whatever is in my hand,' and he divorces her by khula, but there was nothing in her hand, then nothing is obligatory upon her, because she did not deceive him by specifying wealth. The word 'ma' (whatever) is general and includes both wealth and non-wealth. Therefore, she is not considered to have deceived her husband by mentioning wealth, and if she is not deceitful, she is not a guarantor for anything.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage presents a specific case in khula: if the wife initiates khula by offering 'whatever is in my hand' (mafi yadi) as compensation, but she has nothing in her hand at the time, she owes nothing to the husband. The reason is that the word 'ma' (what) is general and does not specifically indicate wealth. Since she did not explicitly promise wealth, she cannot be held liable. The husband's consent to divorce without compensation is presumed because he accepted the offer without the condition of wealth. This protects the wife from being forced to pay when no specific property was promised.

Key Terms
مافی یدی (ma fi yadi): Literally 'what is in my hand'; a general expression that can refer to any object or possession.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because she intended to pay but could not.
B) Because the word 'ma' is general and does not specify wealth, so there is no deception.
C) Because the husband must prove she had something.
D) Because khula requires a minimum compensation of ten dirhams.

Key Takeaway
When a wife offers khula with a general expression like 'ma fi yadi' and she has nothing, she owes no compensation because the general word does not constitute a promise of specific wealth.

Wife's Khula with No Wealth in Hand
Ruling when wife names invalid khula compensation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a wife specifies 'wealth' in her hand for khula but has nothing, and explain why she must return her dower.

Core Idea
If the wife names invalid compensation, she must return the dower to prevent harm.

When a wife initiates khula by offering 'the wealth in my hand,' the husband agrees expecting some compensation. If there is nothing in her hand, the named compensation fails. This lesson explores the Hanafi reasoning: the husband's consent is conditional on receiving something, and the only feasible compensation that avoids injustice is the return of the dower she actually received.

Guided Path
1
Understand the scenario
The wife says 'divorce me by khula on the wealth in my hand.' The husband agrees. Later it is discovered she has no wealth. Now what should she give?
2
Identify the husband's intention
The husband consented to terminate the marriage only because he expected compensation. He would not agree to dissolve the marriage for free.
His consent is conditional on receiving something.
3
Eliminate impossible compensations
The named item (wealth) is unknown (jahl), so cannot be enforced. Its value is also unknown. The value of bida' (mahr al-mithl) cannot be imposed because in khula, bida' is non-valuable (ghayr mutaqawwim).
Three possibilities are ruled out.
4
Determine the only viable option
The only remaining compensation is the dower (mahr) the wife actually received from the husband. This is certain and removes the harm from him.
This is a qiyas-based derivation: since the agreed compensation fails, we fall back to the original dower.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عورت نے کہا خالعنی علی مافی یدی من مال عورت کے ہاتھ میں کچھ بھی نہیں تھا تو مہر لوٹا نا عورت پر لازم ہے

وان قالت خالعنى على مافى يدى من مال فخالعها فلم يكن فى يدها شيء ردت عليه مهرها لانها سمت مالالم يكن الزوج راضيا بالزوال الابعوض ولا وجه الى ايجاب المسمى وقيمته للجهالة ولا الى قيمة البضع اعنى مهر المثل لانه غير متقوم حالة الخروج فتعین ایجاب ما قام به على الزوج دفعا للضرر عنه

ترجمہ اور اگر عورت نے کہا کہ مجھے ضلع دیدے اس مال پر جو میرے ہاتھ میں ہے پس شوہر نے اس کو ضلع دے دیا حالانکہ عورت کے ہاتھ میں کچھ نہ تھا تو عورت اس کو اپنا مہر واپس کرے اس لئے کہ جب عورت نے مال ذکر کیا ہے تو شوہر بغیر عوض لئے ملک نکاح دور کرنے پر راضی نہیں ہوا اور جہالت کی وجہ سے مسمی اور اس کی قیمت کو واجب کرنے کی کوئی صورت نہیں ہے اور نہ بضع کی قیمت یعنی مہر مثل واجب کرنے کی کوئی وجہ ہے۔ اس لئے کہ حالت خروج میں بضع غیر متقوم ہوتا ہے۔ پس اس کا واجب کرنا معین ہو گیا جتنے میں وہ شوہر کو پڑی ے شوہر سے ضرر دور کرنے کے لئے۔

تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر عورت نے اپنے شوہر سے کہا خالعنى على ما فى يدى من مال پس شوہر نے عورت کو ضلع دے دیا پھر دیکھا تو اس کے ہاتھ میں کچھ نہ تھا تو اس صورت میں عورت اس کو مقدار مہر واپس کرے گی دلیل یہ ہے کہ عورت نے چونکہ مال ذکر کیا ہے اس لئے شوہر بغیر عوض لئے ملک نکاح زائل کرنے پر راضی نہیں ہوگا۔ اور عوض کی چار صورتیں ہیں (۱) مسمی (۲) اس کی قیمت (۳) بضع کی قیمت یعنی مہر مثل (۴) وہ مقدار مہر جو عورت اپنے شوہر سے لے چکی ہے۔ اول کے تین احتمال باطل ہیں۔ کیونکہ مسمی یعنی مافی یدی من مال اور اس کی قیمت ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک مجہول ہے اور یوں بھی کہا جا سکتا ہے کہ جب سمی مجهول ہے تو اس کی قیمت بدرجہ اولی مجهول ہوگی اور بضع کی قیمت یعنی مہر مثل اس وجہ سے واجب نہیں کی
If she says: 'Divorce me by khula on the wealth in my hand,' and he does so, but there was nothing in her hand, she must return her dower (mahr) to him. Because she mentioned wealth, and the husband was not content to remove the marriage bond without compensation. There is no possibility to obligate the named item (musamma) or its value due to ignorance (jahala), nor to obligate the value of bida' (i.e., mahr al-mithl) because bida' is non-valuable at the time of exit. Therefore, the only possibility is to obligate whatever the husband has paid (the dower) to remove harm from him.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage addresses a scenario where the wife specifies 'wealth' (min mal) as the khula compensation, but she has nothing in her hand. Here, the husband consented to divorce only because she promised wealth. Since the specific wealth is unknown (majhul), neither the named item nor its value can be enforced. The value of bida' (mahr al-mithl) cannot be imposed because in khula, bida' is non-valuable. Therefore, the wife must return the dower (mahr) she had received from her husband. This is the only way to avoid injustice to the husband, as he gave up his marital rights under the expectation of compensation. The commentary lists four possible compensations and eliminates three, leaving only the return of dower.

Key Terms
جہالت (jahala): Lack of knowledge regarding the amount or identity of the specified wealth, making the contract term invalid.
مہر مثل (mahr al-mithl): The standard dower of a woman of similar status, which is not applicable to khula because bida' is non-valuable at that point.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because mahr al-mithl is only for new marriages.
B) Because bida' is not a valuable commodity (ghayr mutaqawwim) at the time of khula.
C) Because the wife cannot pay mahr al-mithl.
D) Because the husband did not ask for it.

Key Takeaway
When the wife specifies an unknown or non-existent compensation in khula, the only feasible compensation to return is the dower she received, to avoid harming the husband.

Khul' on Unspecified Property: The Wife's Obligation to Return Mahr
Ruling when wife specifies 'mal' in khul' but has nothing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a wife offers khul' for unspecified property and explain the reasoning (ta'lil) that leads to the return of the mahr.

Core Idea
If a wife specifies property in khul' but has none, she must return the mahr to avoid harm to the husband.

This passage addresses a specific scenario in khul': the wife says 'divorce me for what is in my hand of property,' but she actually has nothing. The husband accepts, expecting compensation, but the specified property is non-existent. How should the husband be compensated? The Hanafi jurist systematically eliminates possible compensations and concludes that the mahr (dower) must be returned. This ruling demonstrates a key feature of Hanafi fiqh: the use of practical reasoning (ta'lil) to prevent harm when a literal application fails.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
The wife explicitly says 'min mal' (of property), and the husband accepts the khul' based on that. However, she has nothing. The husband agreed to dissolve the marriage only in exchange for compensation, but the specified subject is absent.
The key is that the husband's consent is conditional on receiving something.
2
Analyze the Possible Compensations
The author considers four options: (1) enforce the specified property itself, (2) impose its estimated value, (3) use mahr al-mithl (equitable dower), (4) order the return of the mahr she had received. The first two fail because the property is unknown (majhul). The third is rejected because in khul', the wife's right to her mahr (vulva value) is extinguished and is no longer a commodity at the time of dissolution.
Mahr al-mithl is for marriage, not for khul' compensation.
3
Apply the Harm Principle
If no compensation is given, the husband would suffer harm (darar) as he lost the marriage without any return. Since the other options are invalid, the only feasible way to remove harm is to require the return of the mahr that the wife had already taken from the husband.
This is a practical solution (raf' al-darar) typical in Hanafi ta'lil.
4
Conclude the Ruling
Therefore, the wife must return the mahr she received. The ruling is founded on necessity: the husband's consent was for compensation, and the mahr provides a certain, predetermined value that avoids ignorance and prevents harm.
This ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is the mufta bihi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان قالت خالعنى على مافى يدى من مال فخالعها فلم يكن فى يدها شيء ردت عليه مهرها لانها سمت مالالم يكن الزوج راضيا بالزوال الابعوض ولا وجه الى ايجاب المسمى وقيمته للجهالة ولا الى قيمة البضع اعنى مهر المثل لانه غير متقوم حالة الخروج فتعین ایجاب ما قام به على الزوج دفعا للضرر عنه
And if she says: 'Divorce me by khul' for what is in my hand of property,' and he divorces her by khul', while there was nothing in her hand, she returns her dower to him, because she specified property, and the husband was not satisfied with the removal (of the marriage) without compensation. There is no way to impose the named (property) or its value due to ignorance, nor to impose the value of the vulva, meaning the mahr al-mithl, because it is not a commodity at the time of exit (khul'). So the imposition of what the husband incurred (the dower) is determined, to remove harm from him.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This is a further ruling in the chapter of Khul'. Here, the wife explicitly says 'min mal' (of property) when offering khul', but she has nothing. The husband accepts and dissolves the marriage. The ruling is that the wife must return the mahr she received (the dower paid by the husband at marriage). The reasoning: By specifying property, the husband implicitly agreed to dissolve only for compensation. Since the specific property is unknown (majhul), it cannot be enforced. Mahr al-mithl (the equitable dower) is not appropriate because the wife's right to the mahr (vulva value) is not a commodity at the time of khul' (it ceases upon dissolution). Therefore, the only way to prevent harm to the husband is to require the wife to return the mahr she already took. The author analyzes four possibilities: (1) the named property (invalid due to ignorance), (2) its value (also ignorant), (3) mahr al-mithl (inapplicable), (4) the actual mahr (valid). This is a typical Hanafi ta'lil (reasoning) based on preventing harm and practical feasibility.

Key Terms
مهر (mahr): The dower paid by the husband to the wife in marriage. In this context, the wife must return it.
مهر مثل (mahr al-mithl): The equitable dower equivalent to what women of similar status receive. Here it is rejected as a basis for compensation in khul'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a wife says 'khul' me for what is in my hand of property' but has nothing, what must she return according to the Hanafi school?
A) The value of the specified property.
B) Mahr al-mithl.
C) The mahr she received.
D) Three dirhams.

Key Takeaway
When a wife specifies property in khul' but has no actual property, the Hanafi school rules that she must return the mahr to compensate the husband, because the other possible compensations are invalid due to ignorance or inapplicability.

Khul' with Void Condition: The Absconding Slave Case
Ruling on khul' with an absconding slave and a void condition of immunity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on khul' with an absconding slave and explain why a void condition does not invalidate the contract.

Core Idea
A void condition in khul' does not void the contract; the missing compensation is due.

Khul' is a divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation. Sometimes the compensation is unconventional, like an absconding slave, and the wife may add conditions like immunity from liability. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling: the condition is void, but the khul' remains valid. Understanding this separation is key to Hanafi contract theory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Conditions
Read the passage and note the act: khul' where the compensation (badal) is an absconding slave, and the wife stipulates she is immune from liability for the slave.
The slave is missing, making delivery uncertain.
2
Isolate the Void Condition
The condition of immunity (barā'ah) from liability contradicts the nature of an exchange contract. Identify why it is fasid (void).
Exchange contracts require the compensation to be safe and deliverable.
3
State the Consequence of the Condition
The condition is void; the wife does not gain immunity. She must deliver the slave if able, otherwise its value.
4
Identify the Dalil (Proof)
The text gives the reason: 'because it is a contract of exchange, so it requires the compensation to be safe.' Recognize this as a legal principle (talil).
This is a general principle applicable to all mu'awadat.
5
Apply the Hanafi Rule on Void Conditions
The khul' itself remains valid because void conditions do not invalidate the main contract. This is a key Hanafi doctrine, also applied in marriage.
The contract is upheld; only the condition is struck.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان اختلعت على عبد لها ابق على انها بريئة من ضمانه لم تبر أو عليها تسليم عينه ان قدرت و تسلیم قیمته ان عجزت لانه عقد المعاوضة فيقتضى سلامة العوض واشتراط البراءة عنه شرط فاسد فيبطل الا ان الخلع لا يبطل بالشروط الفاسدة وعلى هذا النكاح
And if she enters khul' on a slave of hers who has absconded, on the condition that she is immune from liability for him, she is not immune. It is upon her to deliver his essence if she is able, and to deliver his value if she is unable, because it is a contract of exchange, so it requires the compensation to be safe (deliverable). The stipulation of immunity from it is a void condition, so it is nullified. However, the khul' is not invalidated by void conditions, and likewise marriage.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This ruling deals with khul' where the compensation (badal) is an absconding slave (a slave who has run away). The wife stipulates that she is free from liability for the slave (i.e., she won't be responsible if the slave is lost). The ruling: The condition is void (fasid). The wife is not immune; she must deliver the actual slave if she can find him, or if she cannot, she must pay his value (qimah). The reason: Khul' is a contract of exchange (mu'awadah), and the basic requirement is that the compensation be deliverable or safe (salāmah al-‘iwad). A condition that exempts the giver from liability contradicts the nature of the contract and is fasid (void). However, following the Hanafi principle that void conditions do not invalidate the underlying contract (here khul'), the khul' itself remains valid, but the condition is struck down. The same principle applies in marriage (nikah): a void condition in a marriage contract does not invalidate the marriage. This is a key Hanafi doctrine: contracts are valid despite fasid conditions, unless the condition itself is prohibited by a decisive text.

Key Terms
عبد آبق (abd ābiq): A slave who has escaped or run away from his owner.
شرط فاسد (shart fāsid): A void condition that contradicts the essential requirements of the contract. Here, the condition of immunity from liability is void.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The khul' is invalid because the slave cannot be delivered.
B) The khul' is valid but the condition is void; she must deliver the slave or its value.
C) The khul' is valid and she is immune.
D) The khul' is suspended until the slave is found.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a void condition in khul' does not invalidate the divorce; the compensation must still be delivered.

Proportional Payment for Partial Execution of Divorce Request
Ruling on woman who asks for three divorces for 1000, husband gives one

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule of proportional division of countervalue in a conditional divorce request to calculate the amount due.

Core Idea
Each divorce carries a proportional share of the lump sum payment.

This passage addresses a specific scenario in khul' and talaq: a woman offers a sum for three divorces, but the husband only gives one. The ruling hinges on the linguistic function of the preposition 'ba' and how countervalues attach to counterobjects. Understanding this principle helps you calculate the exact obligation in such conditional divorce requests.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
What is the legal consequence when the husband gives only one of the requested three divorces? The woman owes one-third of the thousand.
2
Identify the proof (dalil)
The proof is linguistic: the preposition 'ba' indicates the countervalue. Since she said 'three (divorces) for a thousand', each divorce is valued at one-third.
3
Analyze the division principle
The countervalue is divided proportionally over the counterobjects. Here, the counterobjects are divorces. This is an application of the rule that 'ba' attaches the payment to each item equally unless specified otherwise.
4
Apply to the scenario
If only one divorce is executed, she pays one-third. If two, she pays two-thirds. If three, she pays the full thousand.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا قالت طلقني ثلثا بالف فطلقها واحدة فعليها ثلث الألف لانها لما طلبت الثلث بالف فقد طلبت كل واحدة بثلث الألف وهذا لان حرف الباء تصحب الاعواض والعوض ينقسم على المعوض والطلاق بائن لوجوب المال
And if she says: 'Divorce me three (times) for one thousand,' and he divorces her once, then she owes one-third of the thousand, because when she requested the three for a thousand, she requested each (divorce) for one-third of the thousand. And this is because the letter 'ba' accompanies countervalues, and the countervalue is divided over the counterobjects, and the divorce is ba'in due to the obligation of wealth.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage gives a ruling and its proof. The ruling: if a woman says to her husband 'talliqni thalatha bi-alif' (divorce me three times for one thousand), and the husband gives her only one divorce, she must pay one-third of the thousand (i.e., 333.33 dirhams). The proof: the preposition 'ba' (bi) in 'bi-alif' indicates the countervalue ('iwad). Since she explicitly linked three divorces to the sum of one thousand, it implies each divorce is valued at one-third of that amount. Moreover, the countervalue ('iwad) is divisible over the counterobjects (the divorces). The divorce is ba'in because it involves the payment of wealth (mal), which makes it irrevocable. So if only one divorce is executed, she owes the corresponding portion. The author notes that Imam Shafi'i held this view. The husband may either accept this portion or demand the full amount if he divorces all three later.

Key Terms
بالباء (bi al-ba'): The preposition 'ba' (with) used to indicate the countervalue in a transaction or khul'.
طلاق بائن (talaq ba'in): An irrevocable divorce that ends the marriage immediately, requiring a new contract for remarriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a woman says 'talliqni thalatha bi-alif' and the husband divorces her once, how much must she pay?
A) Full 1000
B) One-third (333.33)
C) Half (500)
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
When a woman requests multiple divorces for a lump sum, each divorce executed carries a proportional share of the payment due to the linguistic implication of 'ba'.

Khul' with a Runaway Slave and Invalid Condition of Exemption
Ruling on khul' with a fasid condition and validity of contract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a fasid condition is included in khul' and explain why the khul' remains valid despite the condition.

Core Idea
A fasid condition does not invalidate khul'; only the condition is void, and the wife must deliver the consideration or its value.

In khul', a wife may offer compensation to obtain a divorce. But what if she offers a runaway slave and stipulates she is not responsible for delivering it? The Hanafi school addresses this with a key principle about commutative contracts: khul' is like a sale requiring sound consideration, and a condition contradictory to that is null, but the contract stands.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the condition
Recognize that the act is khul' (divorce by mutual consent with compensation from the wife). The condition is that the wife is exempt from delivering the runaway slave (i.e., she is not liable if the slave is not found).
The slave is specified as the consideration (iwad).
2
Classify khul' as a commutative contract
Understand that in Hanafi fiqh, khul' is a commutative contract ('aqd mu'awadah) like a sale. Therefore, it inherently requires the consideration to be sound (salim) and deliverable.
This is the basis for the ruling.
3
Apply the rule on fasid conditions
The condition of exemption contradicts the requirement of sound consideration, making it a fasid (corrupt) condition. However, in Hanafi law, a fasid condition in a commutative contract does not invalidate the contract itself; only the condition is void.
Exception: some contracts like marriage are not commutative, but khul' is.
4
Derive the consequence
Since the khul' remains valid, the wife must deliver the specified slave if she can, or its market value if she cannot. The condition of exemption is ignored.
The same analogy applies to marriage (nikah) if the dower is a runaway slave.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الخلع
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد پنجم ضلع عقد معاوضہ ہے۔لہذا سلامت عوض کا تقاضا کرے گا اور اس سے بری ہونے کی شرط لگانا شر طرفا رو و باطل ہو جائے گی مگر یہ کہ ضلع شروط فاسدہ سے باطل نہیں ہوتا ہے اور اسی پر نکاح کو قیاس کیا جائے۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر عورت نے اپنے شوہر سے ایسے غلام پر ضلع کرایا کہ وہ غلام بھا گا ہوا ہے اس شرط پر کہ وہ عورت اس غلام کی ضمانت سے بری ہے یعنی عورت نے یہ شرط بیان کی کہ اس غلام کو حاصل کرنے اور سپرد کرنے کا مجھ سے مطالبہ نہ کیا جائے اگر وہ غلام مل گیا تو سپر د کر دیا جائے گاور نہ کوئی چیز واجب نہ ہوگی تو اس صورت میں یہ عورت بری نہیں ہوگی بلکہ اگر یہ عورت اس غلام پر قادر ہوگئی تو بعینہ اس غلام کو سپر د کرنا واجب ہوگا اور اگر اس غلام کو سپرد کرنے سے عاجز ہوگئی تو اس کی قیمت کا سپر د کرنا واجب ہوگا۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ ضلع عقد معاوضہ ہے اس لئے سلامت عوض کا مقتضی ہو گا لہذا عورت کی جانب سے برات کی شرط لگا نا شرط فاسد ہے یونکہ یہ شرط مقتضی عقد کے خلاف ہے اور چونکہ ضلع شروط فاسدہ کی وجہ سے باطل نہیں ہوتا بلکہ شرط فاسد باطل ہو جاتی ہے اس لئے یہاں شرط باطل ہو جائے گی اور خلع باقی رہے گا۔
اور جب شرط برات باطل اور ضلع صحیح ہے تو عورت پر عبد سمی واجب ہو گا اور اگر عبد مسمی سپرد کرنے پر قادر نہ ہو تو اس کی قیمت واجب ہوگی ۔
اور یہی تفصیل نکاح میں ہے یعنی اگر کسی شخص نے کسی عورت سے نکاح کیا اور مہر بنایا بھاگے ہوئے غلام کو اور شوہر نے اس غلام کو سپرد کرنے سے بری ہونے کی شرط بھی بیان کی تو یہ شخص بری نہیں ہوگا، بلکہ اگر عین غلام پر قادر ہو گیا تو اس کو سپر ذکر نا واجب ہے ، ورنہ اس کی قیمت واجب ہوگی ۔
Chapter of Khul'. Ashraf al-Hidayah, Urdu commentary of Hidayah, volume five. Khul' is a commutative contract. Therefore it requires soundness of the consideration, and stipulating exemption from it is a [؟] condition and becomes void, except that khul' is not invalidated by corrupt conditions. And analogy is made upon this for marriage.
Explanation: The scenario is that if a woman makes khul' with her husband for a slave who has run away, on the condition that she is exempt from liability for that slave, i.e., the woman stipulates that she should not be demanded to obtain and deliver the slave; if the slave is found, he will be delivered, otherwise nothing is obligatory. Then in this case, this woman is not exempt. Rather, if she becomes able to obtain that slave, it is obligatory to deliver the very same slave, and if she is unable to deliver that slave, it is obligatory to deliver its price. The proof is that khul' is a commutative contract, therefore it requires soundness of the consideration. Hence, the condition of exemption on the part of the woman is a fasid condition because it contradicts the requirement of the contract. And since khul' is not invalidated by fasid conditions but the fasid condition becomes void, here the condition becomes void and the khul' remains. And when the condition of exemption is void and the khul' is valid, the named slave is obligatory upon the woman, and if she cannot deliver the named slave, its price is obligatory. And the same detail applies in marriage: if a person marries a woman and makes the dower a runaway slave, and the husband also stipulates exemption from delivering that slave, then this person is not exempt. Rather, if he becomes able to obtain the very slave, it is obligatory to deliver it, otherwise its price is obligatory.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Sharh of Al-Hidayah. It addresses a specific case in khul' where the wife offers a runaway slave as the consideration (iwad) and stipulates that she is not responsible for delivering it. The commentary explains that khul' is a commutative contract ('aqd mu'awadah), which by its nature requires that the consideration be sound and deliverable. Therefore, any condition that contradicts this requirement—such as a stipulation exempting the wife from liability for the slave—is a fasid (corrupt) condition. However, unlike some contracts, khul' is not rendered void by the inclusion of a fasid condition; rather, the condition itself is nullified, while the khul' remains valid. Consequently, the wife must deliver the specified slave if she can, or its market value if she cannot. The commentary then analogizes this to marriage, where if the husband makes the dower (mahr) a runaway slave and stipulates exemption from delivery, the same ruling applies. This reflects the Hanafi principle that in commutative contracts, the consideration must be assured, and stipulations to the contrary are ineffective.

Key Terms
خلع (khul'): A divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation to the husband, considered a commutative contract.
شرط فاسد (shart fasid): A condition that contradicts the requirement of the contract but does not invalidate the contract itself in the case of khul'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case described, what is the ruling if the wife stipulates exemption from delivering the runaway slave in khul'?
A) The condition is valid and the wife is exempt.
B) The condition is fasid but the khul' is valid; the wife must deliver the slave or its price.
C) The khul' is invalid because of the condition.
D) The condition is valid only if the husband agrees.

Key Takeaway
In khul', a fasid condition does not invalidate the contract; the condition is void and the wife must deliver the consideration or its value.

Khul' with Preposition 'بألف' – Proportional Payment
Ruling on khul' using 'bā' for compensation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of proportional division of compensation when the wife uses the preposition 'bā' in khul', and state the resulting ruling.

Core Idea
When the wife uses 'bā' for compensation, the total amount is divided proportionally over the divorces, so executing fewer divorces reduces the payment.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in khul' where the wife phrases her offer using the preposition 'bā' to indicate the exchange. The central question is: if she asks for multiple divorces for a lump sum but the husband gives only one, how much is owed? The Hanafi ruling hinges on the linguistic function of 'bā', which attaches the compensation to each object of exchange proportionally.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling
Read the passage: the wife says 'Divorce me three times for a thousand.' The husband gives one divorce. The ruling is that one ba'in divorce occurs and one-third of the thousand is owed.
The ruling is clear: proportional share is due.
2
Understand the linguistic principle
The preposition 'bā' (ب) in Arabic indicates exchange (mu'awadah). When the wife says 'ثلاثا بالف', the 'bā' attaches the thousand to all three divorces as compensation.
This principle contrasts with other particles like 'على' which might imply a different distribution.
3
Apply the principle of division
Since the compensation (thousand) is attached to the objects (three divorces), it is divided equally. Each divorce gets one-third of the thousand. Thus, when only one divorce is executed, one-third is due.
This is based on the rule: al-iwad yanqasim 'ala al-mu'awwad.
4
Determine the type of divorce
A divorce in exchange for wealth (khul') results in a ba'in (irrevocable) divorce, not raj'i. Hence, the divorce is ba'in.
This is standard Hanafi position for khul'.
5
Confirm the authority
The text from Al-Hidayah presents this as the relied-upon (mufta bihi) view, attributed to the Zahir al-Riwayah. It is also noted that Imam al-Shafi'i holds the same view, making it muttafaq alayh.
No intra-Hanafi dispute is recorded in this passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

واذا قالت طلقني ثلثا بالف فطلقها واحدة فعليها ثلث الألف لانها لما طلبت الثلث بالف فقد طلبت كل واحدة بثلث الألف وهذا لان حرف الباء تصحب الاعواض والعوض ينقسم على المعوض والطلاق بائن لوجوب المال
ترجمہ اور اگر عورت نے کہا مجھے کو تین طلاقیں ایک ہزار کے بدلے دے۔ پس شوہر نے اس کو ایک طلاق دیدی تو عورت پر ایک ہزار کا ایک تہائی واجب ہوگا۔ کیونکہ جب عورت نے ایک ہزار کے بدلے تین طلاقوں کا مطالبہ کیا تو گویا ہر طلاق کو ایک ہزار کے تنہائی کے عوض طلب کیا اور یہ اس لئے کہ لفظ ب عوضوں پر داخل ہوتا ہے اور عوض معوض پر منقسم ہوتا ہے اور طلاق بائن ہوگی مال کے واجب ہونے کی وجہ سے ۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ عورت نے اپنے شوہر سے کہا طلقنی ملا ثا بالف۔ پھر شوہر نے اس کو ایک طلاق دیدی تو عورت پر ایک طلاق بائن واقع ہو جائے گی اور اس پر ایک ہزار کا ایک تہائی واجب ہوگا اور اس کے قائل امام شافعی ہیں دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب عورت نے ایک ہزار کے عوض تین طلاقیں طلب کیں تو گویا اس نے ہر ایک طلاق کو ایک ہزار کے ایک تہائی کے عوض طلب کیا ہے اور اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ کلمہ باعوض پر داخل ہوتا ہے اس وجہ سے الف ( ایک ہزار ) عوض ہوگا اور تین طلاقیں معوض ہوں گی اور قاعدہ ہے کہ عوض معوض پر منقسم ہوتا ہے لہذا ایک ہزار تین طلاقوں پر منقسم ہو گا۔
اور طلاق بائن اس لئے واقع ہوگی کہ یہ طلاق علی مال ہے اور طلاق علی مال سے طلاق بائن واقع ہوتی ہے۔ اس وجہ سے طلاق بائن واقع ہوگی۔
The woman said: 'Divorce me three times for a thousand.' The husband gave one divorce. One-third of the thousand is obligatory upon the woman.
And when she says: 'Divorce me three times for a thousand,' and he divorces her once, then one-third of the thousand is upon her, because when she requested three for a thousand, she requested each one for one-third of the thousand. This is because the letter 'bā' accompanies compensations, and the compensation is divided over the objects of compensation. And the divorce is ba'in due to the obligation of wealth.
Translation: And if the woman said: 'Give me three divorces in exchange for a thousand,' then the husband gave her one divorce, then one-third of a thousand is obligatory upon the woman. Because when the woman requested three divorces for a thousand, it is as if she requested each divorce for one-third of a thousand. And this is because the word 'bā' enters upon compensations, and the compensation is divided over the objects of compensation. And the divorce is ba'in due to the obligation of wealth.
Explanation: The scenario is that the woman said to her husband: 'Divorce me three times for a thousand.' Then the husband gave her one divorce, then one ba'in divorce occurs upon her, and one-third of a thousand is obligatory upon her. Imam Shafi'i is the proponent of this. The proof is that when the woman requested three divorces for a thousand, it is as if she requested each divorce for one-third of a thousand. The reason is that the word 'bā' enters upon compensation, so the thousand is the compensation and the three divorces are the objects of compensation. The rule is that compensation is divided over the objects of compensation, so the thousand is divided over the three divorces. And the divorce is ba'in because this is a divorce for wealth, and a divorce for wealth results in a ba'in divorce. For this reason, a ba'in divorce occurs.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the matn of Al-Hidayah and its commentary. It deals with the case where the wife uses the preposition 'bā' (ب) to indicate the compensation in khul'. The ruling is that if she says 'divorce me three times for a thousand' and the husband gives only one divorce, she owes one-third of the thousand and receives a ba'in divorce. The reasoning is linguistic: the preposition 'bā' in Arabic is used to indicate the means or exchange, so the thousand (the compensation, 'iwad) is attached to all three divorces (the object of compensation, mu'awwad). Since compensation is divided proportionally over the objects, each divorce is considered to have one-third of the thousand as its price. Thus, when only one divorce is executed, one-third of the thousand is due. The divorce is ba'in (irrevocable) because it is a divorce in exchange for wealth, which under Hanafi law makes it irrevocable. The commentary notes that Imam Shafi'i also holds this view, but this is actually the Hanafi position as well, as it is the relied-upon view in the Hidayah. The key principle here is that the particle 'bā' in contractual language indicates compensation and leads to proportional division.

Key Terms
باء (bā): The Arabic preposition used in this context to indicate the exchange (compensation) in a contractual offer, leading to proportional division of the compensation over the objects.
طلاق بائن (talaq ba'in): An irrevocable divorce that ends the marriage immediately without the right of return (ruju') during the 'iddah, unless a new marriage contract is made.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if the wife says 'give me three divorces for a thousand' and the husband gives one divorce?
A) The divorce does not occur because the request was for three.
B) One ba'in divorce occurs and the wife owes one-third of the thousand.
C) One raj'i divorce occurs and the wife owes nothing.
D) The entire thousand is owed because the contract was for three.

Key Takeaway
The preposition 'bā' in khul' divides the compensation proportionally, so paying a fraction of the agreed sum for fewer divorces is valid and results in a ba'in divorce.

Condition vs Compensation: The Meaning of 'على' in Khul'
Intra-Hanafi dispute on 'على' in khul'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the interpretation of 'على' in khul' and apply the thamarah al-khilaf to distinguish the two resulting rulings.

Core Idea
The word 'على' can indicate condition or compensation — the entire ruling for both parties depends on which meaning is adopted.

This lesson examines a classic intra-Hanafi dispute over one word: 'على'. When a wife requests divorce 'على ألف', does she mean 'on condition of a thousand' or 'in exchange for a thousand'? Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn arrive at different conclusions, affecting whether the divorce is raj'i (revocable) or ba'in (irrevocable) and whether any money is owed. Understanding this linguistic and legal analysis is essential for grasping how language drives fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The wife says: 'طلّقني ثلاثاً على ألف' (Divorce me three times on a thousand). The husband gives only one divorce. What is the ruling?
This is the standard case that triggers the dispute.
2
State the two rulings
Abu Hanifa: one raj'i divorce, no compensation. Sahibayn: one ba'in divorce in exchange for one-third of the thousand.
The practical difference is whether the husband can take the wife back without a new contract and whether she pays.
3
Analyze the linguistic argument for condition
Abu Hanifa argues that 'على' indicates a condition, citing Quran 60:12 ('يُبَايِعْنَكَ عَلَىٰ أَن لَّا يُشْرِكْنَ'). It is originally for obligation but borrowed for condition because a condition is linked to the consequence.
Since 'على' expresses condition, the thousand is a condition for all three divorces; if only one is given, the condition is unfulfilled, so no wealth is owed.
4
Analyze the linguistic argument for compensation
The Sahibayn argue that in commutative contracts, 'على' is equivalent to 'باء' (for compensation). They cite everyday usage: 'احمل هذا الطعام بدرهم' and 'على درهم' are synonymous.
Thus, the thousand is compensation divided proportionally over the divorces. One divorce triggers one-third, and the divorce is ba'in because it is compensatory.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Abu Hanifa: wife owes nothing, divorce is raj'i. Under Sahibayn: wife owes one-third, divorce is ba'in. The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is generally Abu Hanifa's view.
The dispute also aligns external schools: Ahmad agrees with Abu Hanifa; Shafi'i agrees with the Sahibayn.

عورت نے کہا طلقنی علی الف شوہر نے ایک طلاق دیدی عورت پر کچھ لا زم ہوگا یا نہیں اور شوہر کو رجوع کا حق ہوگا یا نہیں ، اقوال فقہاء
وان قالت طلقني ثلثا على الف فطلقها واحدة فلاشيء عليها عند ابي حنيفة ويملك الرجعة وقالاهی واحدة بائنة بثلث الألف لان كلمة على بمنزلة الباء فى المعاوضات حتى ان قولهم احمل هذا الطعام بدرهم او علی درهم سواء وله ان كلمة على للشرط قال الله تعالى يبايعنك على ان لا يشركن بالله شيئاً ومن قال لامرأته انت طالق على ان تدخلى الداركان شرطا وهذا لانه اللزوم حقيقة واستعير للشرط لانه يلازم الجزاء واذا كان للشرط فالمشروط لا يتوزع على اجزاء الشرط بخلاف الباء لانه للعوض على مامر واذا لم المال كان مبتداً فوقع الطلاق ويملك الرجعة
يجب
ترجمہ اور اگر عورت نے کہا مجھ کو ایک ہزار پر تین طلاقیں دیدے پس شوہر نے اس کو ایک طلاق دیدی تو ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک عورت پر کچھ واجب نہیں ہوگا اور شوہر رجعت کا مالک ہوگا اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ ایک بائنہ ایک ہزار کے تہائی کے بدلے واقع ہوگی کیونکہ کلمہ علی معاوضات میں باء کے مرتبہ میں ہے حتی کہ ان کا قول احمل هذا الطعام بدرهم يا على درهم دونوں برابر ہیں اور امام صاحب کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ کلمہ علی شرط کے لئے آتا ہے۔ اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے وہ عورتیں آپ سے اس شرط پر بیعت کریں کہ وہ اللہ کے ساتھ کسی کو شریک نہیں کریں گی اور جس شخص نے اپنی بیوی سے کہا است طالق على ان تدخلى الدار تو یہ شرط ہے اور یہ اس لئے کہ کلمہ علی حقیقتاً لزوم کے لئے ہے اور شرط کے لئے مستعار لیا گیا کیونکہ شرط ملازم جزا ہے اور جب (کلمہ علی) کے لئے ہے تو مشروط اجزاء شرط پر منقسم نہیں ہوتا۔ بخلاف باء کے اس لئے کہ وہ عوض کے لئے آتا ہے چنانچہ گزر چکا اور جب مال واجب نہیں ہوا تو یہ طلاق ابتد ا ہو گی پس طلاق پڑ جائے گی اور شوہر رجعت کا مالک ہوگا۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر عورت نے اپنے شوہر سے کہا طلقني ثلاثاً على الف درهم پس شوہر نے اس کو ایک طلاق دیدی تو امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک ایک طلاق رجعی واقع ہو جائے گی اور عورت پر کچھ واجب نہیں ہوگا اور اسی کے قائل امام احمد ہیں اور صاحبین نے فرمایا ہے کہ ایک ہزار درہم کے ایک تہائی کے عوض ایک طلاق بائن واقع ہوگی اس کے قائل امام شافعی ہیں ۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ طلاق علی مال عورت کی جانب سے عقد معاوضہ ہے اور معاوضات میں کلمہ علی با کے مرتبہ میں ہے یعنی عقد معاوضہ میں جو حکم کلمہ بار کا ہے وہی کلمہ علی کا ہے۔ چنانچہ طلقنی ثلاثا بالف کی صورت میں اگر شوہر ایک طلاق واقع کر دیتا تو ایک ہزار کے ایک تہائی کے عوض ایک طلاق بائن واقع ہو جاتی اسی طرح علی الف کی صورت میں بھی ایک طلاق بائن ثلث الف کے عوض واقع ہو جائے گی ۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس جگہ کلمہ علی شرط کے لئے ہے کیونکہ کلمہ علی موضوع ہے معنی استعلاء کے لئے جیسے زید علی اسطح اور اگر
The woman said: 'Divorce me on a thousand.' The husband gave one divorce. Will anything be obligatory upon the woman, and will the husband have the right of return? Statements of the jurists.
And when she says: 'Divorce me three times on a thousand,' and he divorces her once, then nothing is upon her according to Abu Hanifa, and he has the right of return. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: it is one ba'in divorce for one-third of the thousand, because the word 'alā' is in the place of 'bā' in compensations, such that their saying 'carry this food for a dirham' or 'on a dirham' are the same. And according to him (Abu Hanifa), the word 'alā' is for condition. Allah said: 'They pledge allegiance to you on [condition] that they do not associate anything with Allah.' And whoever says to his wife: 'You are divorced on condition that you enter the house,' that is a condition. This is because [the word 'alā'] is really for [the meaning of] obligation, but is borrowed for condition because the condition is connected to the consequence. And when it is for condition, the conditioned thing is not distributed over the parts of the condition, unlike 'bā' because it is for compensation as explained. And when wealth is not obligatory, this divorce becomes initial (without compensation), so the divorce occurs and he has the right of return.
Translation: And if the woman said: 'Give me three divorces on a thousand,' then the husband gave her one divorce, then according to Abu Hanifa nothing is obligatory upon the woman, and the husband will have the right of return. And the two companions said: one ba'in divorce occurs for one-third of the thousand, because the word 'alā' in compensations is of the rank of 'bā', such that their saying 'carry this food for a dirham' or 'on a dirham' are equal. And the proof of Imam (Abu Hanifa) is that the word 'alā' comes for condition. Allah said: 'They pledge allegiance to you on condition that they do not associate anything with Allah.' And whoever says to his wife: 'You are divorced on condition that you enter the house,' that is a condition. This is because the word 'alā' in reality is for [the meaning of] obligation and is borrowed for condition, because the condition is connected to the consequence. And when it is for condition, the conditioned thing is not distributed over the parts of the condition, unlike 'bā' because it is for compensation as has passed. And when wealth is not obligatory, this divorce is initial, so the divorce occurs and the husband has the right of return.
Explanation: The scenario is that if the woman said to her husband: 'Divorce me three times on a thousand dirhams,' then the husband gave her one divorce, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa one raj'i divorce occurs and nothing is obligatory upon the woman, and Imam Ahmad is also of this view. And the two companions said: one ba'in divorce occurs for one-third of a thousand dirhams, and Imam Shafi'i is of this view. The proof of the two companions is that divorce for wealth is a commutative contract from the woman's side, and in compensations, the word 'alā' is of the rank of 'bā'. That is, in a commutative contract, the ruling of the word 'bā' is the same as that of 'alā'. Thus, in the case of saying 'divorce me three times by a thousand,' if the husband executes one divorce, one ba'in divorce occurs for one-third of the thousand. Similarly, in the case of 'on a thousand,' one ba'in divorce for one-third of the thousand would occur. The proof of Imam Abu Hanifa is that here the word 'alā' is for condition, because the word 'alā' is placed for the meaning of elevation (isti'la'), like 'Zaid is on the roof,' and if...
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage presents a significant intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the meaning of the preposition 'alā' (على) in the context of khul'. The issue arises when the wife says to her husband: 'Divorce me three times on a thousand dirhams' (using 'alā' instead of 'bā'). If the husband then gives only one divorce, what is the ruling?

Imam Abu Hanifa holds that nothing is obligatory upon the wife, and the divorce is raj'i (revocable), meaning the husband has the right of return (ruju'). His reasoning is that the word 'alā' in this context indicates a condition (shart), not a compensation. He cites the Quranic verse 'They pledge allegiance to you on condition that they do not associate anything with Allah' (60:12), where 'alā' introduces a condition. Similarly, when someone says to his wife 'You are divorced on condition that you enter the house,' it is a condition. Linguistically, 'alā' originally means 'obligation' (luzum) but is borrowed for condition because a condition is necessarily linked to its consequence (jaza'). Since it indicates a condition, the compensation (the thousand) is not divided over the divorces; rather, it is a condition for the fulfillment of all three divorces. If only one divorce is given, the condition is not fulfilled, so no wealth is owed, and because no wealth was exchanged, the divorce is considered initial (ibtida'i) and thus raj'i.

The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), on the other hand, hold that 'alā' in commutative transactions is equivalent to 'bā' and thus indicates compensation. They reason that just as in the phrase 'carry this food for a dirham' or 'on a dirham' are synonymous, so too does 'alā' function as 'bā' in exchanges. Therefore, the thousand is compensation divided over the three divorces, and if one divorce is given, one-third of the thousand is owed, and the divorce is ba'in (irrevocable).

The commentary also notes that Imam Shafi'i agrees with the Sahibayn, while Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal agrees with Abu Hanifa. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is generally the view of Imam Abu Hanifa in this case, as the text indicates that his proof is stronger based on the linguistic analysis of 'alā' as indicating condition.

Key Terms
على (alā): A preposition that can mean 'on', 'for', or 'on condition of'; the dispute centers on whether it functions as 'bā' (compensation) or as 'shart' (condition).
شرط (shart): A condition that is attached to a contract or statement, often introduced by 'alā'. In this case, the condition is the payment of the thousand for the completion of three divorces.
طلاق رجعی (talaq raj'i): A revocable divorce where the husband has the right to return to his wife during the 'iddah without a new contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what is the ruling if the wife says 'طلّقني ثلاثاً على ألف' and the husband gives one divorce?
A) One ba'in divorce occurs and the wife owes one-third of the thousand.
B) One raj'i divorce occurs and the wife owes nothing.
C) The divorce does not occur because the request was for three.
D) Three divorces occur and the wife owes the entire thousand.

Key Takeaway
The interpretation of a single preposition ('على') can change the entire legal outcome—condition vs compensation—and this intra-Hanafi dispute illustrates the centrality of linguistic analysis in fiqh.

Wife Requests Three Divorces for 1000: Partial Execution by Husband
Ruling and intra-Hanafi dispute on partial execution of khul' offer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling when a wife requests multiple divorces for a payment and the husband gives only one, and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
A partial divorce does not trigger proportional payment; the condition of the wife's request is not met.

When a wife proposes a khul‘ for three divorces but the husband gives only one, does she owe money? The Hanafi school is split on this issue. The difference hinges on the linguistic interpretation of the particle ‘alā. This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning of Imam Abu Hanifa and his two companions, and identifies the relied-upon position for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the point of disagreement
The wife says 'Divorce me three times for one thousand' and the husband gives only one divorce. The dispute concerns whether the wife owes money and whether the divorce is raj‘ī or bāʾin.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and his evidence
Abu Hanifa holds that the wife owes nothing and the divorce is one raj‘ī divorce. His evidence is linguistic: ‘alā in this context indicates a condition (sharṭ), not compensation. He cites Quran 60:12 where ‘alā is used for a condition.
The conditioned (three divorces) does not distribute over parts of the condition.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their evidence
The Sahibayn (Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad) hold that one bāʾin divorce occurs for one-third of the thousand. They argue that ‘alā in commutative contracts is like ‘bi’, making the compensation divisible.
They analogize to saying 'carry this food for a dirham' being equivalent to 'upon a dirham'.
4
Apply the Hanafi principle that ‘alā indicates condition
Abu Hanifa's view is that the original meaning of ‘alā is obligation, but it is borrowed for condition due to the necessary connection between condition and consequence. When used for condition, the conditioned (divorce) is not distributed over parts of the condition (number of divorces).
Since the condition (three divorces) was not fulfilled, no money is owed.
5
Determine the practical consequence and the muftā bihī
Under Abu Hanifa, the husband can take her back without a new contract (raj‘ī). Under the Sahibayn, the divorce is bāʾin and the husband must pay one-third. The relied-upon position is Abu Hanifa's.
The thamarah al-khilaf affects the husband's right to return and financial liability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان قالت طلقني ثلثا على الف فطلقها واحدة فلاشيء عليها عند ابي حنيفة ويملك الرجعة وقالاهي واحدة بائنة بثلث الألف لان كلمة على بمنزلة الباء فى المعاوضات حتى ان قولهم احمل هذا الطعام بدرهم او علی درهم سواء وله ان كلمة على للشرط قال الله تعالى يبايعنك على ان لا يشركن بالله شيئاً ومن قال لامرأته انت طالق على ان تدخلى الداركان شرطا وهذا لانه اللزوم حقيقة واستعير للشرط لانه يلازم الجزاء واذا كان للشرط فالمشروط لا يتوزع على اجزاء الشرط بخلاف الباء لانه للعوض على مامر واذا لم المال كان مبتداً فوقع الطلاق ويملك الرجعة
And if she said: 'Divorce me three times for one thousand,' and he divorced her once, then nothing is incumbent upon her according to Abu Hanifa, and he has the right to take her back. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: It is one irrevocable divorce for one-third of the thousand, because the word 'ala' is like 'bi' in commutative contracts, such that their saying 'Carry this food for a dirham or upon a dirham' are equivalent. And for him (Abu Hanifa) is that the word 'ala' is for condition. Allah Most High said: 'They pledge to you upon [the condition] that they will not associate anything with Allah.' And one who says to his wife: 'You are divorced upon the condition that you enter the house,' that is a condition. This is because [the word 'ala'] is originally for obligation, and it is borrowed for condition because it necessitates the consequence. And when the money is not obligatory, then the divorce is initiated, so the divorce occurs and he has the right to return.

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a khul' offer where the wife says: 'Divorce me three times for one thousand dirhams,' and the husband only gives one divorce. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the wife owes nothing and the husband retains the right to take her back (talāq rajʿī). The two companions (Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad) hold that one irrevocable divorce (bāʾin) occurs for one-third of the thousand. The difference turns on the interpretation of the particle 'alā'. The Sahibayn argue that 'alā' in commutative contracts functions like 'bi', making the compensation divisible. Abu Hanifa argues that 'alā' in such contexts indicates a condition (sharṭ), not a direct exchange. The husband did not condition the divorce on full payment but rather made the divorce conditional on the wife's request; since the condition was not fully met, no money is owed. The divorce is thus initiated by the husband alone and remains rajʿī. The text also cites the Quranic verse (al-Mumtaḥanah 12) where 'alā' is used for a condition, supporting Abu Hanifa's view. Note that 'alā' can have multiple meanings: literal superiority, obligation, or condition. Here, the context of a request with a monetary reference leads to the conditional meaning.

Key Terms
على (ʿalā): In this passage, the particle 'alā' is analyzed as either indicating a condition (sharṭ) or compensation (ʿiwaḍ).
طلاق بائن (ṭalāq bāʾin): An irrevocable divorce that ends the marriage immediately, requiring a new contract for remarriage.

Key Takeaway
When a wife offers payment for multiple divorces and the husband gives only one, the Hanafi muftā bihī is that no payment is due and the divorce is rajʿī.

Partial Execution of Delegated Triple Divorce
Ruling on partial delegated divorce with conditional payment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a wife partially executes a delegated triple divorce and explain the logical basis: the husband's conditional consent.

Core Idea
If the husband delegates three divorces for a fee, and she gives one, no divorce occurs—his consent was conditional on the full amount.

The previous lesson covered the case where the wife initiates the offer. Here, the husband is the delegator. The ruling differs because the consent belongs to the husband, and he did not agree to any separation without receiving the full payment. We will examine the reasoning and contrast the two scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
The husband says: 'Divorce yourself three times for 1000.' The wife divorces herself once. According to the Hanafi school, no divorce occurs; the marriage remains intact.
The wording 'bi-alf' or 'ala-alf' both indicate a condition of payment.
2
Locate the Dalil (Rational Proof)
The text provides the reasoning: the husband was not satisfied with irrevocability (baynuna) unless he receives the entire 1000 dirhams. Since the condition is not fulfilled, the divorce is ineffective.
The proof is aqli (rational) based on the nature of conditional consent.
3
Contrast with the Wife's Offer Scenario
In the previous case, the wife said: 'Divorce me three times for 1000.' There, the wife was willing to become ba'in for the full amount, so she is satisfied with a portion (one divorce) a fortiori. Here, the husband's consent is restrictive.
The difference hinges on who is the offeror: the wife's offer shows her willingness to accept less; the husband's offer shows his unwillingness.
4
Formalize the Qiyas (Analogy)
The asl (original case) is the wife's offer: partial execution is valid because her consent covers the full amount. The far' (new case) is the husband's delegation: partial execution is invalid because his consent is specifically tied to the full amount. The illa (effective cause) is the conditionality of consent on the full payment.
This is a qiyas ma'a al-fariq (analogy with a difference) that results in opposite rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و لو قال الزوج طلقى نفسك ثلثا بالف او على الف فطلقت نفسها واحدة لم يقع شيء لان الزوج مارضى بالبينونة الاليسلم الالف كلها بخلاف قولها طلقى ثلثا بالف لانهالمارضيت بالبينونة بالف فكانت ببعضها ارضى
And if the husband said: 'Divorce yourself three times for one thousand or upon one thousand,' and she divorced herself once, nothing occurred because the husband was not satisfied with irrevocability unless the entire thousand is delivered to him, unlike her saying: 'Divorce me three times for one thousand,' because she was satisfied with irrevocability for one thousand, so she is satisfied with a portion of it a fortiori.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on delegated divorce (tafwīḍ). If the husband authorizes his wife to divorce herself three times in exchange for 1000 dirhams, and she only divorces herself once, no divorce takes place. The reason is that the husband's consent to become irrevocably separated (bāʾin) is conditional upon receiving the full 1000 dirhams. Since only a partial attempt was made, his condition is not fulfilled, and the divorce does not occur. This contrasts with the previous scenario where the wife initiated the offer: there, the wife was willing to become bāʾin for 1000, so by giving one divorce, the husband implicitly accepts a lesser exchange. But here, the husband is the delegator; he did not consent to any separation without the full amount. Therefore, the wife's single divorce is ineffective. Note that the husband's phrase 'bi-alf' (with one thousand) or 'ala alf' (upon one thousand) both indicate a condition of payment.

Key Terms
تفويض (tafwīḍ): The act of the husband delegating the wife to divorce herself.
بينونة (baynūna): Irrevocable separation; a divorce that ends the marriage without the possibility of remarriage without a new contract.
شرط (sharṭ): Condition; a stipulation that must be fulfilled for the divorce to take effect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) One rajʿī divorce occurs with no payment.

The Meaning of 'Ala in Khul' Contracts
Explaining the legal meaning of 'ala as condition rather than compensation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the use of 'ala as a condition (shart) versus compensation ('iwad) in khul' and conditional talaq.

Core Idea
'Ala in khul' indicates a condition; divorce takes effect only when the condition is fulfilled.

In Hanafi fiqh, the particle 'ala (على) carries distinct legal meanings depending on context. In khul' and conditional talaq, understanding whether 'ala introduces a condition or a compensation is critical to determining when the divorce occurs. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi position that 'ala in such contexts primarily indicates a condition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term and its context
Locate 'ala in the source text and note whether it appears in a khul' or conditional talaq phrase.
The particle is often followed by 'an' or a noun phrase.
2
Distinguish between condition and compensation
Determine if 'ala introduces a prerequisite (condition) or an exchange (compensation). The Hanafi view: it is a condition unless specified otherwise.
In khul', the husband receives compensation, but the word 'ala itself does not denote that.
3
Examine the Quranic proof
Read the verse 60:12 where 'ala appears in a pledge on condition of avoiding shirk. This shows 'ala can indicate a condition.
The verse: يبايعنك على أن لا يشركن بالله شيئاً
4
Apply to the example
Analyze the example 'You are divorced on condition that you enter the house.' The divorce is suspended until entry.
The condition must be clearly stated after 'ala.
5
Note practical implications
If 'ala is misinterpreted as compensation, the divorce might be considered immediate, which is incorrect in Hanafi law.
This affects timing of 'iddah and other rights.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ان علمیہ علی الشرط الکفایہ [؟] 
يبايعنك على أن لا يشركن بالله شيئاً 
أنت طالق على أن تدخلي الدار
['Knowledge is only by the condition of sufficiency?'] 
They pledge allegiance to you on condition that they do not associate anything with Allah 
You are divorced on condition that you enter the house.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage discusses the legal meaning of the word 'ala (على) in the context of khul'. The author explains that 'ala can indicate either obligation (الإلزام) or condition (الشرط). In khul', if 'ala is used in a way that connotes a condition, it is taken as such because of the natural relationship between condition and result. The author cites a supposed principle (perhaps from the matn) that 'ala is real for condition, and a Quranic verse (60:12) where 'ala appears in the pledge of allegiance on condition of avoiding shirk. An example is given: 'You are divorced on condition that you enter the house.' This establishes that 'ala in khul' indicates a condition, which has implications for when the divorce occurs.

Key Terms
على (ala): A particle that can mean either compensation (عوض) or condition (شرط) in legal contexts.
