اپنے او پر بدل خلع کو لازم کرنا صیح ہے تو باپ جو بھر پور شفقت رکھتا ہے اس کا اپنے اوپر بدل خلع کو لازم کرنا بدرجہ ولی صبح ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ صغیرہ کا مہر ساقط نہیں ہوگا اگر چہ خلع مہر کو ساقط کر دیتا ہے اس لئے کہ مہر باپ کی ولایت کے تحت داخل نہیں ہے کیونکہ مہر ساقط کرنے میں صغیرہ پر کوئی شفقت نہیں حالانکہ ولایت کا مبنی ہی شفقت ہے۔
Chapter of Khul': If a husband gives khul' for one thousand on the condition that the girl's father is a guarantor, then the khul' takes effect and the thousand is obligatory upon the father. And if he gives her khul' for one thousand on the condition that he is a guarantor, then the khul' is valid and the thousand is upon the father, because stipulating the compensation of khul' upon a stranger is valid, so upon the father it is more appropriate. And her mahr is not waived because it is not under the father's guardianship. Translation: And if the husband gave khul' to his own [wife] for one thousand dirhams on the condition that the wife's father is the guarantor of this property, then the khul' takes effect and one thousand dirhams become obligatory upon the father, because stipulating compensation of khul' upon a stranger is valid, so stipulating it upon the father is valid as a priority, and the woman's mahr is not waived because it is not included under the father's guardianship. Explanation: The scenario is that if the husband gave khul' to his minor wife for one thousand dirhams with the condition that the wife's father is guarantor of this one thousand, then in this case the khul' takes effect and one thousand dirhams become obligatory upon her father, and here 'guarantee' means undertaking the property upon himself, not being a surety on behalf of the minor, because the husband does not have entitlement to property from the minor such that someone could be surety on her behalf. The proof of the mentioned ruling is that stipulating compensation of khul' upon a stranger is valid, therefore stipulating the compensation upon the father is valid as a priority. The author of 'Inayah, mentioning the reason for priority, wrote: The father has guardianship of disposal over the property of his minor child, so the father can conduct transactions like purchase, sale, lease, and deposit of his minor child's property, whereas no stranger is allowed these disposals. Then stipulating the compensation of khul' upon himself is also a disposal. So when a stranger who has no guardianship over general disposals is allowed to bind himself to the compensation of khul', then the father who has guardianship over general disposals is a fortiori permitted to bind himself to the compensation of khul'. A second reason for priority is that khul' is a transaction that revolves between benefit and harm, so when a stranger whose compassion is deficient is allowed to bind himself to the compensation of khul', then the father who has abundant compassion is a fortiori allowed to bind himself to the compensation of khul'. The author of Hidayah says: The minor's mahr is not waived even though khul' normally waives the mahr, because the mahr is not within the father's guardianship, since waiving the mahr does not involve compassion for the minor, while guardianship is based on compassion.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the khul' of a minor wife where the father acts as guarantor for the compensation. The author states the ruling: the khul' is valid and the father is liable for the specified amount. The proof is based on the principle that stipulating compensation on a stranger (ajnabi) is valid in Hanafi fiqh, and since the father is closer to the child than a stranger, it is a fortiori valid. The commentary expands with two reasons for this priority (olawiyyah): first, the father has general guardianship (wilayah) over the minor's property, unlike a stranger; second, the father's compassion (shafaqah) is greater. The author also clarifies that 'guarantee' means the father undertakes the liability on himself, not as a surety on behalf of the minor, because the husband cannot claim property from the minor directly. Additionally, the mahr of the minor wife is not waived by the khul' because the father's guardianship does not extend to waiving the mahr, as that would not be compassionate towards the minor. This point is from the Hidayah itself.

Key Terms
خلع (khul'): Divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation paid by her to the husband.
صغیرہ (ṣaghīrah): A minor female who has not reached puberty.
ضامن (ḍāmin): A guarantor who undertakes liability for a debt or obligation.
مہر (mahr): Dowry or bridal gift given by the husband to the wife.
ولایت (wilāyah): Guardianship or authority over a minor's affairs.
اولویت (awlawiyyah): Priority; a fortiori reasoning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the khul' of a minor wife where the father is guarantor, why is the mahr not waived?
A) Because the father's guarantee covers the mahr as well.
B) Because the mahr is not within the father's guardianship to waive.
C) Because the minor wife did not accept the khul'.
D) Because the husband did not stipulate the mahr in the khul'.

Key Takeaway
The father's guarantee in khul' of a minor wife is valid by qiyas awlawi, but his guardianship does not extend to waiving her mahr.

Khul' of a Minor Wife: Acceptance, Liability, and the Father's Role
Explains khul' depending on minor's acceptance and two narrations on father's acceptance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on khul' when the compensation is conditioned upon a minor wife and explain why the father's acceptance is subject to two narrations.

Core Idea
A minor can accept khul' to effect divorce but cannot be liable for compensation; the father's acceptance is valid only in one narration.

This lesson explores the Hanafi rulings on khul' (divorce by redemption) involving a minor wife. When compensation is conditioned on the minor herself, the validity hinges on her acceptance, but she is not financially liable. The father's acceptance on her behalf introduces an intra-madhhab difference with two narrations, grounded in whether the acceptance is viewed as pure benefit or akin to a conditional oath.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The text presents two situations: (1) khul' with a specific compensation conditioned on the minor, and (2) khul' in exchange for her mahr when the father is not a guarantor. Both follow the same rules regarding acceptance and liability.
Focus on the first scenario for now; the second is a variant.
2
Determine the ruling on minor's acceptance
If the minor is capable of acceptance (understands the contract), her acceptance validly effects divorce, but the compensation is not obligatory because a minor lacks legal capacity for financial liability (ahl al-gharamah).
This is the core ruling on which both narrations agree.
3
Understand the two narrations on father's acceptance
If the father accepts on her behalf, there are two narrations: one deems it valid (as pure benefit like a gift), the other invalid (as it resembles a conditional oath which cannot be delegated).
The text does not specify which is mufta bihi, but the reasoning is based on the nature of the acceptance.
4
Apply the principle of shart yamin
In the second narration, the acceptance is likened to a conditional oath (shart yamin) because the khul' is contingent on the condition. Such personal oaths cannot be performed by a deputy, hence the father's acceptance is ineffective.
This is a key usul point within the Hanafi school.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if father's acceptance is valid, divorce occurs without any compensation due; if invalid, no divorce occurs unless the minor herself accepts.
This highlights the importance of the ruling for fatwa.

تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر شوہر نے اپنی صغیرہ بیوی کو ضلع دیا اس کے مہر پر اور باپ اس مہر کا ضامن نہیں ہوا تو بھی اس صغیرہ کے قبول کرنے پر موقوف ہے۔ پس اگر صغیرہ نے قبول کر لیا تو طلاق پڑ جائے گی اس لئے کہ شرط پائی گئی اور چونکہ صغیرہ اہل تاوان میں سے نہیں ہے اس لئے مہر ساقط نہیں ہوگا۔ اور اگر صغیرہ کی طرف سے باپ نے قبول کیا تو اس صورت میں دو روایتیں ہیں۔ ایک روایت کے مطابق صحیح ہوگا اور ایک کے مطابق صحیح نہیں اور دونوں روایتوں کی وجہ سابق مسئلہ میں گزر چکی ۔
If the husband made the thousand conditioned upon the minor, then the khul' depends on her acceptance if she is capable of acceptance. If she accepts, the divorce occurs due to the condition being met, but the property is not obligatory because she is not capable of liability. Then if the father accepts on her behalf, there are two narrations. Translation: And if the husband conditioned the thousand dirhams upon the minor, then (the validity of khul') depends on the minor's acceptance, provided she is capable of acceptance. So if the minor accepts, the divorce occurs because the condition is met, but the property is not obligatory because the minor is not capable of liability. Then if the father accepted the compensation on her behalf, there are two narrations. Explanation: The scenario is that if the husband conditioned the thousand dirhams compensation upon his minor wife, then the validity of khul' depends on this minor's acceptance, provided she is capable of acceptance, i.e., she understands the contract and knows that through khul' the marriage is dissolved and she gets freedom, but has to pay property. So if the minor accepted, the divorce occurs because the condition of acceptance is met, but the property is not obligatory because the minor is not capable of liability. And if the father accepted on behalf of this minor, then there are two narrations: in one narration this acceptance is valid, and in another narration it is not. The reason for the first narration is that this acceptance is pure benefit for the minor—she gets freedom from the husband without paying property—so it is like accepting a gift on her behalf. The reason for the second narration is that this acceptance is in the nature of a conditional oath (shart yamin), and a conditional oath does not admit deputyship. Also, if the husband gave khul' to the minor in exchange for her mahr, and the father did not guarantee the mahr, then it depends on her acceptance. So if she accepts, she is divorced and the mahr is not waived. If the father accepts on her behalf, then there are two narrations. Translation: And similarly, if the husband gave khul' to the minor in exchange for her mahr and the father did not guarantee the mahr, it depends on her acceptance. So if she accepts, the divorce occurs and the mahr is not waived. And if the father accepted on her behalf, then there are two narrations. Explanation: The scenario is that if the husband gave khul' to his minor wife in exchange for her mahr and the father did not guarantee this mahr, then it also depends on this minor's acceptance. So if the minor accepted, the divorce occurs because the condition is met, and since the minor is not capable of liability, the mahr is not waived. And if the father accepted on behalf of the minor, then in this case there are two narrations: according to one narration it is valid, and according to another it is not valid, and the reason for both narrations has passed in the previous issue.

Commentary
This passage contains two rulings with proofs about khul' of a minor wife where the compensation is conditioned either as a specific amount or as her mahr, and the father is not a guarantor. The first ruling: if the husband conditions the compensation upon the minor herself, the khul' is contingent upon her acceptance. If she accepts (and is capable of doing so), the divorce takes effect because the condition is fulfilled, but the compensation is not obligatory because a minor is not legally capable of financial liability (gharamah). If the father accepts on her behalf, there are two narrations within the Hanafi school: one considers it valid because it is a pure benefit for the minor (like accepting a gift), while the other considers it invalid because the acceptance is akin to a conditional oath (shart yamin) which cannot be delegated. The second ruling parallels the first but with the compensation being her mahr. If the father is not a guarantor, the same conditions apply: the khul' depends on her acceptance, and if she accepts, divorce occurs but the mahr is not waived. The father's acceptance again has two narrations with the same reasoning. The passage does not specify which narration is relied upon, but the principle that a minor cannot be liable for compensation is consistent throughout.

Key Terms
قبول (qabūl): Acceptance; here it refers to the minor's or father's acceptance of the khul' offer.
روایت (riwāyah): Narration or transmission of a legal ruling within the school.
شرط یمین (shart yamīn): A conditional oath; a statement that makes the occurrence of talaq conditional on something.
تاوین (tāwīn): Liability for compensation; the minor is not 'ahl al-gharamah' (capable of liability).

Father's Guarantee of Mahr in Khul' of Minor Wife
Ruling on father's liability for mahr in minor's khul' with istihsan vs qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a father's liability when he guarantees the mahr in a khul' of a minor wife, and distinguish between the qiyas and istihsan positions.

Core Idea
Istihsan halves the father's liability for mahr in a minor's khul' before consummation.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in family law: a father guarantees the mahr as compensation for khul' of his minor daughter. The source presents a ruling that by strict analogy (qiyas) the father owes the full mahr, but by juristic preference (istihsan) only half is due. Understanding this distinction illustrates how Hanafi jurists balance textual analogy with equitable considerations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? The father guaranteeing the mahr in khul' of a minor wife. The ruling: the khul' is valid (wife divorced), and by istihsan the father is liable for half the mahr.
The text states the wife is divorced because the father's acceptance fulfills the condition.
2
Locate the proof
The proof is qiyas (analogy) to the case of a major wife who does khul' before consummation for an amount equal to her mahr.
The asl (original case) is the major wife; the far' (new case) is the father as guarantor.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the analogy work? The common factor (illa) is compensation for release from marriage before consummation. In the major wife's case, by qiyas she owes the full mahr, but by istihsan she owes half. The same illa applies to the father's guarantee, so the same reduction applies by istihsan.
The illa is khafiyyah (hidden), requiring istihsan to override the apparent qiyas.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Is there disagreement? The Hanafi school relies on istihsan for this ruling. Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may reject istihsan and hold the father liable for the full amount.
The text indicates the istihsan ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is the mufta bihi position.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Why is istihsan preferred? Because before consummation, the benefit of marriage is incomplete, so compensation is halved as a matter of fairness. This is applied equally to the father as guarantor.
The text does not elaborate on the rationale, but it is a well-known Hanafi principle in khul' cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اگر باپ مہر کا ضامن ہو گیا عورت مطلقہ ہو جائے گی
وان ضمن الاب المهر وهو الف درهم طلقت لوجود قبوله وهو الشرط ويلزمه خمس مائة استحسانا وفى القياس يلزمه الالف واصله فى الكبيرة اذا اختلعت قبل الدخول على الف ومهرها الف ففى القياس عليها
ترجمہ اور اگر باپ مہر کا ضامن ہو گیا اور وہ مہر ایک ہزار درھم ہے تو عورت طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی اس لئے کہ باپ کی طرف قبول پایا گیا اور وہی شرط ہے اور استحسانا پانچ سو لازم ہوں گے اور قیاس کے تحت پورا ہزار لازم ہوگا اور اس کی اصل بڑی عورت میں ہے کہ جب اس نے داخول سے پہلے ایک ہزار پر خلع کیا اور اس کا مہر ایک ہزار ہے تو قیاساٌ اس پر پورا ہزار ہے۔
If the father became the guarantor of the mahr, the woman becomes divorced. And if the father guaranteed the mahr, and it is one thousand dirhams, she is divorced because his acceptance is found, and that is the condition, and he is liable for five hundred by istihsan, and by qiyas he is liable for the full thousand. Its origin is in the case of a major wife: if she does khul' before consummation for one thousand, and her mahr is one thousand, then by qiyas the full thousand is upon her.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This is a brief ruling with proof concerning the situation where the father guarantees the mahr (which is one thousand dirhams) as the compensation for khul' of a minor wife. The ruling: the wife is divorced because the father's acceptance (indirectly) fulfills the condition. However, the liability of the father is reduced: by istihsan (juristic preference), he owes only five hundred dirhams, whereas by qiyas (analogy) he would owe the full thousand. The basis for the istihsan is analogized to the case of a major wife who initiates khul' before consummation with a mahr of one thousand and agrees to pay one thousand; by qiyas she would owe the full thousand, but the Hanafi school applies istihsan to reduce it to half (five hundred). The same reduction is applied here to the father as guarantor. The text does not elaborate on the reason for istihsan in the original case, but it is a well-known Hanafi principle that in khul' before consummation, the compensation is often halved due to the principle of 'iwad (compensation) being proportionate to the benefit received. The father's liability is thus reduced by analogy.

Key Terms
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference; a method of departing from strict qiyas in favor of a more equitable ruling.
قیاس (qiyās): Analogical deduction; extending a ruling from an original case to a new case based on a common illa.
مہر (mahr): Dowry; here it is the amount specified in the marriage contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because the minor wife waived half of her mahr.
D) Because the father's guarantee was conditional on half payment.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when a father guarantees mahr for a minor's khul' before consummation, he owes only half by istihsan, overturning the qiyas ruling of full liability.

Khula' of Minor Wife with Father as Guarantor: Istihsan vs Qiyas
Ruling with proof by istihsan overriding qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for khula' of a minor wife with a father guarantor and explain why istihsan overrides qiyas.

Core Idea
In khula' before consummation, the husband's intent to cancel debt limits the father's guarantee to half the mahr.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah addresses a specific scenario: the husband gives khula' to his minor wife in exchange for her mahr (1000 dirhams), and the father guarantees this amount. The wife is non-consummated. According to strict analogy (qiyas), the father would owe the full 1000 dirhams. However, Hanafi jurists prefer istihsan (juristic preference), resulting in the father owing only 500 dirhams. This lesson unravels the reasoning behind the preferred ruling and the principle that custom and intent override literal analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the transaction
The husband gives khula' to his minor wife on the condition of her mahr (1000 dirhams). The minor's father guarantees the mahr. The wife is non-consummated (ghayr madkhul biha).
2
State the Hanafi ruling (istihsan)
According to the mufta bihi (zahir al-riwayah) position, the father owes 500 dirhams, and the wife owes nothing extra. This is because after talaq before consummation, the wife is entitled to half the mahr (500), so the khula' is effectively for that amount.
The matn says: 'five hundred extra, and according to istihsan nothing is due from her.'
3
Contrast with the qiyas ruling
Qiyas would require the father to pay the full 1000 dirhams, analogizing to the case of an adult woman who takes khula' on her full mahr (1000) before receiving it: she must return half (500) plus an extra 500 to complete the 1000 she undertook.
The original case (asl) is the adult woman; the new case (far') is the minor with father as guarantor.
4
Identify the illa (effective cause) for istihsan
The husband's customarily intended goal is to be free from the entire mahr obligation. Since after talaq before consummation, the wife only retains half the mahr, returning that half achieves the husband's intent. The father's guarantee is interpreted as covering only what is actually due from the wife.
The illa is khafiyyah (hidden), determined by tahqiq al-manat (investigation of the rationale).
5
Evaluate the authority and application
The istihsan ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah (the six core books) and is mufta bihi. The commentator (Ashraf al-Hidayah) follows al-Marghinani. This ruling is specific to non-consummated marriage; if consummation had occurred, different rules apply.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خمس مائة زائدة و فى الاستحسان لا شئى عليها لانه يراد به عادة حاصل ما يلزم لها

ترجمہ اور اگر صغیرہ کا باپ مہر کا ضامن ہو گیا اور وہ ہزار درہم ہیں تو عورت طالقہ ہو جائے گی اس لئے کہ باپ کا قبول کرنا پایا گیا اور یہی شرط تھی اور باپ پر پانچ سو درہم لازم ہوں گے اور یہ استحسان ہے اور قیاس کا تقاضا ہے کہ ایک ہزار لازم ہوں اور اس مسئلہ کی اصل بالغہ عورت کے حق میں ہے جب کہ اس نے دخول سے پہلے ایک ہزار پر ضلع لیا حالانکہ اس کا مہر بھی ایک ہزار درہم ہے۔ پس قیاس کا تقاضا ہے کہ اس پر پانچ سو درہم زائد لازم ہوں اور استحسان کا تقاضا ہے کہ اس پر کچھ واجب نہ ہو۔ کیونکہ ایسے خلع سے عادتاً اس چیز کا حاصل ہونا مراد ہوتا ہے جو عورت کے لئے لازم ہے۔

تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر شوہر نے اپنی صغیرہ بیوی کو اس کے مہر پر یعنی مقدار مہر پر ضلع دیا اور صغیرہ کا باپ اس مقدار مہر کا ضامن ہو گیا اور وہ مہر ایک ہزار درہم ہیں تو اس صغیرہ پر طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی کیونکہ باپ کا قبول کرنا پایا گیا اور یہی شرط تھا۔ اور صغیرہ کے باپ پر استحسانا پانچ سو درہم لازم ہوں گے دلیل یہ ہے کہ مسئلہ اس صورت میں فرض کیا گیا جب کہ صغیرہ غیر مدخول بہا ہو اور مہر ایک ہزار ہے پھر خلع منسوب کیا گیا ہے اس کے مہر کی طرف اور اس کا مہر وہ ہے جو اس عورت کے واسطے نکاح کی وجہ سے واجب ہوا ہے اور عورت کے واسطے طلاق قبل الدخول کی صورت میں نصف مہر واجب ہوتا ہے اور نصف مہر پانچ سو درہم ہیں ۔ بس گو یا شوہر نے اپنی بیوی سے پانچ سو درہم پر خلع کیا ہے اس وجہ سے اس صغیرہ کے باپ پر پانچ سو درہم لازم ہوں گے اور قیاس کا مقتضی یہ ہے کہ اس پر ایک ہزار درہم لازم ہوں گے۔ اس مسئلہ کی اصل بالغہ عورت میں ہے کہ جب بالغہ عورت نے دخول سے پہلے ایک ہزار پر ضلع لیا حالانکہ اس کا مہر بھی ایک ہزار ہے اور عورت نے ابھی تک مہر پر قبضہ نہیں کیا ہے تو اس صورت میں قیاس یہ ہے کہ عورت پر اس کے شوہر کے لئے پانچ سو درہم واجب ہوں ۔ کیونکہ طلاق قبل الدخول کی وجہ سے پانچ سو درہم اس کے شوہر کے ذمہ سے ساقط ہو گئے ہیں اور عورت نے ایک ہزار درہم کا التزام کیا ہے اور عورت کے ذمہ سے نصف یعنی پانچ سو درہم ساقط ہو گئے ہیں۔ بطریق مقاصد کیونکہ نصف مہر ساقط ہونے کے بعد بھی عورت کے لئے اس کے شوہر پر پانچ سو درہم باقی رہ گئے تھے ۔ لہذا ایک ہزار پورا کرنے کے لئے عورت پر پانچ سو درہم مزید واجب ہوں گے اور استحسان یہ ہے کہ عورت پر کچھ واجب نہ ہو۔ کیونکہ شوہر کا مقصود یہ ہے کہ اس کے ذمہ سے کل مہر ساقط ہو جائے اور یہ مقصود حاصل ہو چکا ہے اس لئے عورت پر مزید کچھ واجب نہ ہوگا۔ واللہ اعلم با اصواب جمیل احمد عفی عنہ
Five hundred extra, and according to istihsan nothing is due from her because by custom the intent is to obtain that which is due to her. Translation: And if the father of the minor wife became guarantor of the mahr and it is one thousand dirhams, then the woman will be divorced because the father's acceptance is found, and that was the condition. And the father owes five hundred dirhams by istihsan. Qiyas requires one thousand. The original of this issue is in the case of an adult woman when she takes khula' before consummation on one thousand while her mahr is also one thousand dirhams. So qiyas requires that she owes an extra five hundred dirhams, and istihsan requires that nothing is due from her. Because in such khula', customarily the intent is to obtain that which is due to the woman. Explanation: The case is that if the husband gave khula' to his minor wife on her mahr, i.e., on the amount of mahr, and the minor's father became guarantor of that amount, and that mahr is one thousand dirhams, then the minor will be divorced because the father's acceptance occurred, and that was the condition. And by istihsan the minor's father owes five hundred dirhams. The proof is that the case is assumed when the minor is non-consummated and the mahr is one thousand. Then khula' is attributed to her mahr. Her mahr is what is due to her due to marriage. In case of divorce before consummation, half the mahr is due, and half is five hundred dirhams. So as if the husband took khula' from his wife for five hundred dirhams, therefore the father owes five hundred. Qiyas requires one thousand. The original of this issue is in the adult woman: when an adult woman takes khula' before consummation on one thousand while her mahr is also one thousand and she has not yet taken possession of the mahr, then qiyas is that she owes her husband five hundred dirhams because due to divorce before consummation, five hundred dirhams are dropped from the husband's liability, and she undertook one thousand, so half (five hundred) is dropped from her liability. In terms of objectives, after the half mahr is dropped, five hundred dirhams still remained due to her from her husband. So to make it one thousand, she owes an extra five hundred. Istihsan is that nothing is due from her because the husband's intent is that the entire mahr be dropped from his liability, and that intent has been achieved, so nothing extra is due from her. And Allah knows best with correctness. Jameel Ahmad, may he be forgiven.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah explains a specific ruling in khula' when a father guarantees the mahr for his minor daughter. The matn states that in istihsan, nothing extra is due from the wife. The commentary details the scenario: the husband gives khula' to his minor wife for her mahr (1000 dirhams), the father guarantees this amount. The talaq occurs because the father accepted. According to istihsan, the father only owes half the mahr (500 dirhams) because the wife is non-consummated. The reasoning: after talaq before consummation, the wife is entitled to half the mahr (500), so effectively the khula' is for 500 dirhams. Thus the father, as guarantor, owes 500. Qiyas would make the father liable for the full 1000 dirhams, similar to the case of an adult woman who takes khula' before consummation on her full mahr (1000) while she has not yet received it: she owes the husband an extra 500 because she must return the half that he is entitled to. However, istihsan is preferred because the husband's intention in khula' is to be free from any remaining mahr obligation, and that purpose is served by the return of the half she is entitled to. The commentator cites the reasoning and concludes with 'Allah knows best.' No other schools are mentioned; the Hanafi position is presented as istihsan mufta bihi.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): A juristic preference that overrides qiyas due to custom or need, resulting in a different ruling.
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning used to derive a ruling for a new case based on a similar original case with a shared effective cause.
خلع (khul'): Divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation (typically the mahr or part of it).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of a minor wife whose father guarantees her mahr of 1000 dirhams in a khula' before consummation, how much does the father pay according to the Hanafi mufta bihi position?
A) 1000 dirhams
B) 500 dirhams
C) Nothing
D) 250 dirhams

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, upon khula' of a non-consummated minor wife with father as guarantor, the father owes only half the mahr by istihsan, overriding qiyas.

Talaq — Divorce
beginner

Definition and First Ruling of Zihar
Defines zihar, its conditions, cause, and first ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of zihar, identify its conditions and pillar, and explain the ruling that intercourse becomes haram until expiation is performed.

Core Idea
Zihar: a prohibited statement likening the wife to a mahram, causing temporary prohibition removed only by expiation.

Zihar is a pre-Islamic practice that Islam reformed. It is not divorce but a serious sin requiring expiation. This lesson unpacks its definition, conditions, and the immediate legal effect: the wife becomes haram for her husband until he fulfills kaffarah. Understanding this institutes proper therapy for marital disputes.

Guided Path
1
Define zihar lexically and technically
Start with the linguistic meaning (from 'zahr', back) and the Shari'ah definition: likening one's wife to a female mahram. Note the specific phrase 'anti 'alayya ka-zahri ummi' and its equivalents.
The phrase 'ka-zahr ammi' is the key; any substitution with the same meaning also counts.
2
Identify the conditions and pillar of zihar
List the conditions: husband must be sane, adult, Muslim; wife must be his legal wife (mankuhah). The rukn is the utterance of the zihar phrase (or its equivalent).
There is no requirement for intent (niyyah) – the mere utterance triggers the ruling.
3
Understand the cause (sabab) of zihar
The sabab is nushuz (rebellion) of the wife, as illustrated by the story of Khawlah bint Tha'labah and her husband Aws ibn Samit.
The cause is not a condition; zihar can occur even without nushuz, but the revelation addressed that context.
4
State the ruling: prohibition until expiation
The hukm is that intercourse, touching, and kissing become haram until the husband performs kaffarah (freeing a slave, fasting two months, or feeding sixty poor). The marriage remains intact.
The Quranic imperative in 58:3-4 establishes the wujub of expiation before resuming contact.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الظهار
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو بدایہ جلد پنجم
ظہار باب مفاعلت کا مصدر ہے لغوی معنی ہیں مرد کا قول اپنی بیوی سے انت علی کظهر امی اور شریعت میں ظہار کہتے ہیں منکوحہ کو محرمہ اہد یہ کے ساتھ تشبیہ دینا ظہار کی شرط مظاہر کا عاقل بالغ مسلمان ہونا ہے اور عورت کا نسائنا میں سے ہونا یعنی منکوحہ ہونا ہے اور ظہار کا رکن ہے مرد کا اپنی بیوی سے انت علی کظھر امی یا اس کے قائم مقام کوئی لفظ کہنا اور اس کا سبب نشوز ہے اس لئے کہ آیت ظہار خولہ کے بارے میں نازل ہوئی ہے اور در انحالیکہ وہ ناشزہ تھی اور اس کا حکم یہ ہے کہ ولی اور دھراعتی ولی کا حرام ہونا بقاء نکاح کے ساتھ یہاں تک کہ کفارہ ادا کرے۔
عہد رسالت میں اوس بن صامت صحابی نے غصہ میں اپنی بیوی خولہ بنت ثعلبہ کو کہہ دیا کہ تو میرے حق میں ایسی ہے جیسے میری ماں کی پشت کہ مجھ پر حرام ہے۔ اس کے بعد دونوں نادم ہوئے حضرت خولہ چارہ جوئی اور تحقیق حال کے لئے بارگاہ نبوت میں حاضر ہوئیں۔ چونکہ ظہار کے متعلق اب تک کوئی آسمانی حکم نازل نہیں ہوا تھا آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے قوم ہی کے معمول کو قابل عمل خیال کر کے فرما دیا کہ اب تمھارے اور تمھارے شوہر میں اجتماع کی کوئی صورت نہیں ہو سکتی۔ یہ سن کر وہ واویلا کرنے لگیں اور اپنے خاوند کا شکوہ شروع کر دیا اور کہا یا رسول اللہ میری جوانی شوہر ہی کے گھر میں گزری اور جب میں بوڑھی ہو چکی ہوں تو ظہار کر بیٹھا ہے۔ لیکن علیحدگی کی صورت میں گھر تباہ جائے گا اور چھوٹے چھوٹے بچے پر یشان مارے مارے پھریں گے اس کے بعد آسمان کی طرف سر اٹھا کر کہنے لگیں بارالہی! مجھے بیچاری کا تو ہی وارث ہے۔ میری فریاد رسی کر اس وقت سورہ مجادلہ کی ابتدائی آیتیں نازل ہوئیں جن میں ظہار کو طلاق قرار نہ دیا گیا اور فرمایا گیا کہ جس نے جنا نہیں وہ ماں کیونکر ہو سکتی ہے اور اپنی لغویات کے کہنے کا انسداد یہ حکم دے کہ فرمایا کہ جب تک شوہر کفارہ ادا نہ کرے اس وقت تک منکوحہ کے قریب نہ جائے۔ (بیان القرآن)
شوہر نے بیوی کو کہا انت علی کظہر امی عورت مرد پر حرام ہو جائے گی کفارہ ادا کرنے سے پہلے ولی ہمس، اور تقبیل حرام ہے پلمس
واذا قال الرجل لامرأته انت علی کظهر امی فقد حرمت عليه لا يحل له وطيها ولا مسها ولا تقبيلها حتى يكفر عن ظهاره لقوله تعالى والذين يظاهرون من نسائهم الى ان قال فتحرير رقبة من قبل ان يتما ساو الظهار کان طلاقافي الجاهلية فقرر الشرع اصله ونقل حكمه الى تحريم موقت بالكفارة غير مزيل للنكاح وهذا لانه جناية لكونه منكرا من القول وزورا فيناسب المجازاة عليها بالحرمة وارتفاعها بالكفارة ثم الوطى اذا حرم حرم بدواعيه كيلا يقع فيه كما فى الاحرام بخلاف الحائض والصائم لانه يكثر وجود هما فلو حرم الدواعى يفضى الى الحرج ولا کذالک الظهار والاحرام
ترجمہ اور جب مرد نے اپنی بیوی سے انت علی کظیر امی کہا تو یہ عورت اس پر حرام ہوگئی۔ اس کے لئے اس کے ساتھ وطی کرنا حلال نہیں ہے اور نہ اس کو چھونا اور نہ اس کا بوسہ لینا حلال ہے یہاں تک کہ اپنے ظہار کا کفارہ دے کیونکہ اللہ تعالیٰ کا فرمان ہے اور جو لوگ اپنی عورتوں سے ظہار کرتے ہیں یہاں تک کہ فرمایا کہ ایک غلام آزاد کریں جماع سے پہلے اور ظہار زمانہ جاہلیت میں طلاق تھا پھر شریعت نے اس کی اصل کو برقرار رکھا اور اس کا حکم کفارے کے وقت تک تحریم کی طرف منتقل کر دیا درانحالیکہ وہ نکاح کو زائل کرنے والا نہیں ہے اور یہ
Chapter of Zihar. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary, volume five. Zihar is the verbal noun of the form mufa'alah. Lexically, it means a man's statement to his wife: 'You are to me like the back of my mother.' In Shari'ah, zihar is likening a wife to a prohibited mahram. Condition of zihar: the mazhir (husband) must be sane, adult, Muslim, and the wife must be from among his women, i.e., married. The pillar (rukn) of zihar is that the man says to his wife, 'You are to me like the back of my mother' or any word that stands in its place. Its cause is nushuz (rebellion) because the verse of zihar was revealed regarding Khawlah, and she was nashizah. Its ruling is that the wife becomes haram for him in terms of intercourse and its preliminaries, while the marriage remains, until he performs expiation. During the time of the Prophet, Aws ibn Samit, a Companion, said in anger to his wife Khawlah bint Tha'labah: 'You are to me like the back of my mother, i.e., you are haram for me.' Afterwards both regretted. Lady Khawlah approached the Prophet for legal inquiry. Since no divine command had come regarding zihar, the Prophet initially considered the common practice and said that there is no possibility of intercourse between you two. Hearing this, she began to wail and complain about her husband, saying, 'O Messenger of Allah, I spent my youth in his house, and when I have grown old, he committed zihar. But separation would destroy the house and small children would wander.' Then she lifted her head to the sky, saying, 'O Allah, You alone are the inheritor of this poor soul; help me!' At that time, the opening verses of Surah al-Mujadilah were revealed, declaring that zihar is not divorce, and stating: 'How can she be a mother when she did not give birth to him?' And they forbade such statements and commanded that the husband should not approach the wife until he performs expiation. (Bayan al-Quran) If a man says to his wife, 'You are to me like the back of my mother,' the woman becomes haram for the man; intercourse, touching, and kissing are not allowed before expiation. And when a man says to his wife, 'You are to me like the back of my mother,' she becomes haram for him; it is not permissible for him to have intercourse with her, nor to touch her, nor to kiss her until he performs expiation for his zihar, because Allah Almighty says: 'And those who pronounce zihar from among their wives... until they free a slave before they touch each other.' Zihar was a divorce in the Jahiliyyah. Then the Shari'ah established its original form and changed its ruling to a temporary prohibition bound by expiation, without dissolving the marriage. This is because zihar is a crime, being an objectionable and false statement, so the suitable penalty is prohibition and its removal by expiation. Furthermore, when intercourse is prohibited, its preliminaries are also prohibited to prevent falling into it, just as in ihram. This is unlike a menstruating woman or a fasting person, because these conditions occur frequently; if the preliminaries were prohibited, it would lead to hardship. Zihar and ihram are not like that. Translation: And when a man says to his wife 'You are to me like the back of my mother,' this woman becomes haram for him. It is not halal for him to have intercourse with her, nor to touch her, nor to kiss her, until he performs expiation for his zihar, because Allah Almighty says: 'And those who pronounce zihar from among their wives...' until He says 'free a slave before they touch each other.' And zihar was a divorce in the Jahiliyyah. Then the Shari'ah established its original form and transferred its ruling to a temporary prohibition by expiation, without dissolving the marriage.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on Zihar (ظہار) from Ashraf al-Hidayah. It begins with a lexical definition: 'zihar' derives from 'zahr' (back), and the phrase 'anti 'alayya ka-zahri ummi' indicates a prohibition likening the wife to one's mother. The legal definition specifies that zihar is likening one's wife to a mahram female relative. The conditions for zihar are: the husband must be sane, adult, and Muslim; the wife must be his legal wife. The rukn (pillar) is the utterance of the specific phrase or its equivalent. The sabab (cause) is nushuz (rebellion), referencing the incident of Khawlah bint Tha'labah with her husband Aws ibn Samit. The hukm (ruling) is that the wife becomes haram for intercourse and its preliminaries until expiation is performed, while the marriage remains intact. The passage then narrates the story: after the Prophet initially thought zihar was a form of divorce, Khawlah complained to Allah, and the early verses of Surah al-Mujadilah were revealed, clarifying that zihar is not divorce but a sin requiring expiation (freeing a slave before resuming relations). The Arabic text then states the first explicit ruling: if a man says the phrase, she becomes haram for intercourse, touching, and kissing until expiation, based on the Quranic verse. The commentary explains that zihar was a form of divorce in pre-Islamic times, but Islam retained its form while changing the ruling to temporary prohibition (tahrim mu'qqat) conditional on expiation, without dissolving the marriage. This is because it is a false and objectionable statement (munkar min al-qawl wa zur), so the penalty fits the crime: prohibition that is lifted by expiation. The text also compares the prohibition of zihar and ihram to the case of menstruation and fasting, noting that in the latter, the preliminaries are not prohibited because of frequent occurrence leading to hardship, whereas zihar and ihram are rare.

Key Terms
ظہار (zihar): A husband declaring his wife like his mother's back, causing temporary prohibition until expiation.
کفارہ (kaffarah): Expiation required to lift the prohibition of zihar; options: freeing a slave, fasting two months consecutively, or feeding sixty poor.
نشوز (nushuz): Rebellion or disobedience of the wife towards the husband, given as the cause for zihar in the story of Khawlah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position, what is the effect of a husband saying to his wife, 'You are to me like the back of my mother'?
A) The marriage is immediately dissolved
B) The wife becomes permanently haram like a mother
C) Intercourse becomes prohibited until expiation is performed
D) The wife performs khula'

Key Takeaway
Zihar is a prohibited statement that makes the wife haram for intimacy until expiation is performed; it is not a form of divorce.

Definition, Conditions, and Ruling of Zihar
Defines zihar linguistically and legally with conditions and story

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of zihar, identify its conditions, pillar, cause, and ruling, and explain how it differs from divorce.

Core Idea
Zihar is a temporary prohibition requiring kaffarah; it is not divorce.

Zihar is a pre-Islamic practice that Islam reformed into a temporary prohibition with expiation. This lesson defines zihar both lexically and legally, outlines its necessary conditions and pillar, explains its cause (nushuz), and clarifies that it does not dissolve the marriage but prohibits intimacy until kaffarah is performed. The story of Khawlah bint Tha'labah illustrates its revelation context.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Lexical and Legal Definition
Begin by grasping the linguistic origin: 'zihar' comes from 'zahr' (back), and legally means likening one's wife to a female mahram relative (e.g., mother). This distinction is key to understanding its mechanism.
Note that the legal effect is a temporary prohibition, not divorce.
2
Identify the Necessary Conditions (Shurut) and Pillar (Rukn)
List the conditions: the muzahir (man) must be sane, adult, and Muslim; the wife must be married under a valid contract. The rukn is the specific utterance: 'anti alayya ka-zahri ummi' or its substitute.
Without these, the act is not considered zihar legally.
3
Recognize the Cause (Sabab) and Ruling (Hukm)
The cause is nushuz (wife's disobedience) as shown in the story. The ruling is that intimacy becomes haram until the husband performs kaffarah, while the marriage remains intact.
The prohibition is temporary and conditional on kaffarah.
4
Appreciate the Historical Background and Reform
Read the story of Aws ibn Samit and Khawlah. In the Jahiliyyah, zihar was considered divorce. Islam revealed Surah al-Mujadilah to change it to a temporary prohibition with kaffarah, thus reforming a harsh practice.
This shows the gradual regulation of customs through revelation.

باب الظهار
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو بدایہ جلد پنجم
ظہار باب مفاعلت کا مصدر ہے لغوی معنی ہیں مرد کا قول اپنی بیوی سے انت علی کظهر امی اور شریعت میں ظہار کہتے ہیں منکوحہ کو محرمہ اہد یہ کے ساتھ تشبیہ دینا ظہار کی شرط مظاہر کا عاقل بالغ مسلمان ہونا ہے اور عورت کا نسائنا میں سے ہونا یعنی منکوحہ ہونا ہے اور ظہار کا رکن ہے مرد کا اپنی بیوی سے انت علی کظھر امی یا اس کے قائم مقام کوئی لفظ کہنا اور اس کا سبب نشوز ہے اس لئے کہ آیت ظہار خولہ کے بارے میں نازل ہوئی ہے اور در انحالیکہ وہ ناشزہ تھی اور اس کا حکم یہ ہے کہ ولی اور دھراعتی ولی کا حرام ہونا بقاء نکاح کے ساتھ یہاں تک کہ کفارہ ادا کرے۔
عہد رسالت میں اوس بن صامت صحابی نے غصہ میں اپنی بیوی خولہ بنت ثعلبہ کو کہہ دیا کہ تو میرے حق میں ایسی ہے جیسے میری ماں کی پشت کہ مجھ پر حرام ہے۔ اس کے بعد دونوں نادم ہوئے حضرت خولہ چارہ جوئی اور تحقیق حال کے لئے بارگاہ نبوت میں حاضر ہوئیں۔ چونکہ ظہار کے متعلق اب تک کوئی آسمانی حکم نازل نہیں ہوا تھا آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے قوم ہی کے معمول کو قابل عمل خیال کر کے فرما دیا کہ اب تمھارے اور تمھارے شوہر میں اجتماع کی کوئی صورت نہیں ہو سکتی۔ یہ سن کر وہ واویلا کرنے لگیں اور اپنے خاوند کا شکوہ شروع کر دیا اور کہا یا رسول اللہ میری جوانی شوہر ہی کے گھر میں گزری اور جب میں بوڑھی ہو چکی ہوں تو ظہار کر بیٹھا ہے۔ لیکن علیحدگی کی صورت میں گھر تباہ جائے گا اور چھوٹے چھوٹے بچے پر یشان مارے مارے پھریں گے اس کے بعد آسمان کی طرف سر اٹھا کر کہنے لگیں بارالہی! مجھے بیچاری کا تو ہی وارث ہے۔ میری فریاد رسی کر اس وقت سورہ مجادلہ کی ابتدائی آیتیں نازل ہوئیں جن میں ظہار کو طلاق قرار نہ دیا گیا اور فرمایا گیا کہ جس نے جنا نہیں وہ ماں کیونکر ہو سکتی ہے اور اپنی لغویات کے کہنے کا انسداد یہ حکم دے کہ فرمایا کہ جب تک شوہر کفارہ ادا نہ کرے اس وقت تک منکوحہ کے قریب نہ جائے۔ (بیان القرآن)
Chapter of Zihar. Ashraf al-Bidaya, Urdu commentary on al-Hidayah, volume 5. Zihar is a verbal noun from the pattern mufa'alah. Lexically it means a man saying to his wife 'anti alayya ka-zahri ummi' (you are to me like the back of my mother). In Shari'ah, zihar means likening one's married wife to a prohibited woman (like mother). The condition for zihar is that the one performing zihar (muzahir) be sane, adult, and Muslim. The wife must be from among his women, i.e., married to him. The pillar (rukn) of zihar is the man saying to his wife 'anti alayya ka-zahri ummi' or a phrase that substitutes for it. Its cause (sabab) is nushuz (rebellion/disobedience), because the verse of zihar was revealed concerning Khawlah, and she was rebellious (nashizah). Its ruling is that intercourse and its preliminaries become haram while the marriage remains, until he pays kaffarah. In the era of the Prophet (peace be upon him), the companion Aws ibn Samit in anger said to his wife Khawlah bint Tha'labah: 'You are to me like my mother's back, forbidden to me.' After that, both regretted. Khawlah came to the Prophet (peace be upon him) to seek remedy and inquire. Since no divine command had been revealed about zihar, the Prophet (peace be upon him) considered the practice of the people as applicable and said: 'There is no way for you and your husband to come together.' Hearing this, she began to wail and complain about her husband, saying: 'O Messenger of Allah, I spent my youth in my husband's house, and now that I am old, he has made zihar. But in separation, the household will be destroyed and the young children will wander aimlessly.' Then she raised her head to the sky and said: 'O Allah, You alone are my helper, relieve me.' At that time, the early verses of Surah al-Mujadilah were revealed, in which zihar was not considered divorce, and it was said: 'How can she be a mother when she did not give birth to him?' And to prevent verbal offences, the command was given: 'Until the husband pays kaffarah, he should not approach the wife.' (Bayan al-Quran)
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage defines zihar (ظہار), a pre-Islamic Arabian practice that Islam reformed. The lexical meaning comes from 'zahr' (back), and the legal definition is likening one's wife to a female relative who is permanently prohibited (like mother, sister, etc.). The text lists essential conditions: the muzahir must be sane, adult, and Muslim; the wife must be a married woman within the marriage contract. The pillar (rukn) is the specific utterance or its substitute. The cause (sabab) is nushuz (disobedience), illustrated by the story of Khawlah bint Tha'labah, who was described as nashizah. The ruling is that sexual activity and its precursors become haram until kaffarah is paid, while the marriage remains intact. The story emphasizes that zihar was initially treated by the Prophet (peace be upon him) as a permanent separation according to custom, but Allah intervened with revelation that made it a temporary prohibition with kaffarah as a means of expiation. This shows Islamic law's gradual regulation of existing practices.

Key Terms
ظہار (zihar): Verbal noun from mufa'alah; lexically a man saying 'you are like my mother's back'; legally likening one's wife to a mahram relative.
مظاہر (muzahir): The man who performs zihar.
مظاہر منہا (muzahir minha): The wife who is the object of zihar.
کفارہ (kaffarah): The expiation required for zihar: freeing a slave, fasting two consecutive months, or feeding sixty poor persons.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the pillar (rukn) of zihar according to the text?
A) The wife being rebellious (nashizah)
B) The man saying 'anti alayya ka-zahri ummi' or its substitute
C) The payment of kaffarah
D) The presence of witnesses

Key Takeaway
Zihar is a temporary prohibition, not divorce, requiring kaffarah before resuming intimacy.

Ruling of Zihar: Prohibition and Kaffarah
States ruling of zihar with Quranic proof and analogy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of zihar, cite the Quranic proof, and explain why precursors are forbidden analogously to ihram.

Core Idea
Zihar temporarily forbids intimacy until kaffarah, like ihram forbids its precursors.

Zihar is a pre-Islamic practice that Islam reformed into a temporary prohibition linked to expiation. This lesson unpacks the ruling: what becomes haram, the Quranic evidence, and the rationale for forbidding all precursors to intercourse. You will learn why the strictness of zihar mirrors ihram but differs from menstruation and fasting.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling and its scope
Identify the precise acts that become haram upon zihar: intercourse, touching, and kissing. Note that this prohibition is temporary until kaffarah is performed.
The prohibition applies to all forms of intimacy, not just intercourse.
2
Locate the Quranic proof
Find the verse from Surah al-Mujadilah (58:3-4) quoted in the passage. Understand that it commands freeing a slave before touching, establishing the sequence.
The imperative 'fa-tahriru' indicates wujub (obligation).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the verse proves that touching is prohibited before kaffarah. The phrase 'min qabli an yatamassa' explicitly prohibits any contact before expiation.
This is a clear textual indication (dalala qat'iyya).
4
Note the change from jahiliyyah
Recognize that zihar was permanent divorce in pre-Islam. Islam retained the form but changed the legal effect to temporary prohibition with expiation.
This shows the Shari'ah's reform of harmful customs.
5
Evaluate the analogy with ihram
Understand why precursors are forbidden: to prevent falling into the prohibited act itself. This analogy with ihram is contrasted with menstruation/fasting, where forbidding precursors would cause hardship due to frequency.
The rarity of zihar/ihram vs frequency of menstruation/fasting justifies the difference.

شوہر نے بیوی کو کہا انت علی کظہر امی عورت مرد پر حرام ہو جائے گی کفارہ ادا کرنے سے پہلے ولی ہمس، اور تقبیل حرام ہے پلمس
واذا قال الرجل لامرأته انت علی کظهر امی فقد حرمت عليه لا يحل له وطيها ولا مسها ولا تقبيلها حتى يكفر عن ظهاره لقوله تعالى والذين يظاهرون من نسائهم الى ان قال فتحرير رقبة من قبل ان يتما ساو الظهار کان طلاقافي الجاهلية فقرر الشرع اصله ونقل حكمه الى تحريم موقت بالكفارة غير مزيل للنكاح وهذا لانه جناية لكونه منكرا من القول وزورا فيناسب المجازاة عليها بالحرمة وارتفاعها بالكفارة ثم الوطى اذا حرم حرم بدواعيه كيلا يقع فيه كما فى الاحرام بخلاف الحائض والصائم لانه يكثر وجود هما فلو حرم الدواعى يفضى الى الحرج ولا کذالک الظهار والاحرام
ترجمہ اور جب مرد نے اپنی بیوی سے انت علی کظیر امی کہا تو یہ عورت اس پر حرام ہوگئی۔ اس کے لئے اس کے ساتھ وطی کرنا حلال نہیں ہے اور نہ اس کو چھونا اور نہ اس کا بوسہ لینا حلال ہے یہاں تک کہ اپنے ظہار کا کفارہ دے کیونکہ اللہ تعالیٰ کا فرمان ہے اور جو لوگ اپنی عورتوں سے ظہار کرتے ہیں یہاں تک کہ فرمایا کہ ایک غلام آزاد کریں جماع سے پہلے اور ظہار زمانہ جاہلیت میں طلاق تھا پھر شریعت نے اس کی اصل کو برقرار رکھا اور اس کا حکم کفارے کے وقت تک تحریم کی طرف منتقل کر دیا درانحالیکہ وہ نکاح کو زائل کرنے والا نہیں ہے اور یہ

اشرف الهدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد پنجم
اس وجہ سے ہے کہ ظہار جرم ہے کیونکہ یہ قول مخش اور جھوٹ ہے پس مناسب ہے کہ ( مردکو ) اس کہنے پر حرام کئے جانے سے سزادی جائے اور اس حرمت کا دور ہونا کفارہ کے ساتھ ہے پھر جب وہی حرام ہو گئی تو وہ اپنے دوائی کے ساتھ حرام ہو گی تا کہ ولی میں مبتلا نہ ہو جائے جیسے احرام میں ہے برخلاف حائضہ کے اور روزہ دار کے کیونکہ ان دونوں کا وجود بکثرت ہوتا ہے پس اگر دوائی ولی حرام ہوں تو تکلیف تک پہنچا دے گا اور نہار اور حرام کا یہ حال نہیں ہے۔
تشریح مسئلہ پر ہے کہ اگر کسی مرد نے اپنی بیوی سے انت علی کظہر امی کہا تو یہ عورت اس پر حرام ہوگئی ۔ نہ اس کے ساتھ وطی کرنا حلال رہا اور نہ اس کو چھونا اور نہ بوسہ لینا حلال رہا حتی کہ شوہر اپنے ظہار کا کفارہ دیدے۔ دلیل آیت والذين يظاهرون من نسائهم ثم يعودون لما قالوا فتحرير رقبة من قبل ان يتماسا دالكم توعظون به والله بما تعملون خبیر ہے ترجمہ ۔ اور جولوگ
اپنی بیویوں سے ظہار کرتے ہیں پھر اپنی کہی ہوئی بات کی تلافی کرنا چاہتے ہیں تو اسکے ذمہ ایک نام یا لونڈی کا آزاد کرانا ہے۔ قبل اسکے دونوں (میاں بی بی) باہم اختلاط کریں۔ اس سے تم کو نصیحت کی جاتی ہے اور اللہ تعالٰی کو تمھارے سب اعمال کی پوری خبر ہے۔
(حکیم مت)
اس آیت میں تصریح کی گئی ہے کہ اگر ظہار کے بعد رجوع کا ارادہ ہو تو پہلے نام آزاد کرے۔ یعنی کفارہ ظہار ادا کرے پھر جماع اور اس کے متعلقات حلال ہوں گے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ زمانہ جاہلیت میں ظہار طلاق شمار ہوتی تھی یعنی ہیں مل سکان زائل ہو جاتا ہے اور حرمت کو ثابت ہو جاتی ہے اسی طرح ظہار سے نکاح زائل ہو جاتا تھا اور حرمت ثابت ہو جاتی میں ہیں شریعت اسلام نے تمہاری سمیت قبرة او رکھی مگر اس کا حکم بدل دیا۔ چنانچہ فرمایا کہ ظہار سے نکاح تو زائل نہیں ہوتا البتہ کفارہ دینے تک بیوی نے بولی کرنا حرام ہے۔ اور ظہار کی وجہ سے حرمت اس لئے ہے کہ ظہار کرنا جرم ہے اور جرم اس وجہ سے ہے کہ اظہار کرنا ناز یبا اور جھوٹ بات ہے چنانچہ باری تعالیٰ کا ارشاد ہے وانهم ليقولون منكرا من القول وزورا یعنی بلاشبہ وہ لوگ ایک نا معقول اور جھوٹ بات کہتے ہیں (اس لئے گناہ ضرور ہوگا ) ( حضرت تھانوی) پس جب ظہار کرنا خش اور جھوٹ بات ہے تو ایسا کہنے پر اس شخص کو یہ مراد بنا مناسب ہوگا کہ اس کی بیوی کو اس پر حرام کر دیا جائے تا وقتیکہ کفارہ ادا کرے اور وہ جرم کفارہ سے دور ہو جاتا ہے چنانچہ باری تعالی کا ارشادت ان الحسنات يذهبن السیئات اور حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا ہے۔ اتبع الحسنة السيئة تمحها ۔ یعنی برائی کے بعد نیکی کرنا برائی مومنادیتا ہے۔ نہیں جب کفارہ سے جنابت دور ہو گئی تو حرمت بھی ختم ہو جائے گی۔
پھر جب ظہار کی وجہ سے ولی کرنا حرام ہوا تو وہ تمام چیزیں حرام ہو جائیں گی جو دائی الی الویٹی ہیں مثالی عورت کو کچھونا ۔ اس کا بوسہ لینا ، تا کہ یہ چیز میں اس کو وطی میں مبتلا نہ کر دیں، جیسا کہ حالت احرام میں بھی اور دوائی ولی سب حرام ہیں۔ اس کے بر خلاف حائضہ اور روزہ دار ہے چنانچہ حائضہ اور روز جدار عورت کے ساتھ صرف وہی حرام ہے نہ کہ دوائی ولی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حیض اور روزہ کا وجود بار بار ہوتا ہے۔ پس اگر بوسہ وغیرہ کو حرام کیا گیا تو یہ مفضی الی الحرج ہوگا اور رہاظہار اور احرام تو ان کا وقوع بھی کبھار شاذ و نادر ہوتا ہے اس لئے ظہار اور احرام کی حالت میں وطی کے ساتھ دوائی ولی بھی حرام کی کئیں نہیں اور حیض اور روزہ میں دوائی ولی کو حرام نہیں کیا گیا۔
The husband said to the wife: 'You are to me like my mother's back.' The woman will become forbidden to the man; before paying kaffarah, touching and kissing are haram. And if a man says to his wife 'You are to me like my mother's back,' she has become forbidden to him. It is not permissible for him to have intercourse with her, nor to touch her, nor to kiss her, until he makes kaffarah for his zihar, due to the saying of Allah the Exalted: 'And those who make zihar of their women...' until He said: 'So freeing a slave before they touch each other.' Zihar was divorce in the Jahiliyyah, so the Shari'ah established its original form and transferred its ruling to a temporary prohibition linked to kaffarah, not dissolving the marriage. This is because zihar is a crime, as it is an abominable and false statement. So it is appropriate to punish it by prohibition, and its removal by kaffarah. Then when intercourse is forbidden, its precursors are also forbidden to prevent falling into it, as in ihram, unlike the menstruating woman and the fasting person, because their states occur frequently; if precursors were forbidden, it would lead to hardship. This is not the case with zihar and ihram. Translation: And when a man says to his wife 'You are to me like my mother's back,' this woman becomes forbidden to him. It is not halal for him to have intercourse with her, nor to touch her, nor to kiss her, until he gives the kaffarah of his zihar. Because Allah the Exalted says: 'And those who make zihar of their women...' until He said: 'freeing a slave before intercourse.' And zihar in the Jahiliyyah was divorce. Then the Shari'ah kept its original form but transferred its ruling to temporary prohibition with kaffarah, without dissolving the marriage. And this is because zihar is a crime, as it is an abominable and false statement. So it is appropriate that the man be punished by prohibition on account of this saying, and the removal of that prohibition is by kaffarah. Then when intercourse is forbidden, its precursors are also forbidden so that he does not fall into it, as in ihram. Unlike the menstruating woman and the fasting person, because both of these states occur frequently; if precursors were forbidden, it would lead to hardship. This is not the case with zihar and ihram. Then the explanation: The issue is that if a man says to his wife 'You are to me like my mother's back,' this woman becomes forbidden to him. Neither intercourse is permissible, nor touching, nor kissing, until the husband pays the kaffarah of his zihar. The proof is the verse: 'And those who make zihar of their women and then return to what they said, so free a slave before they touch each other. That is what you are admonished with. And Allah is Aware of what you do.' Translation: And those who make zihar of their wives, then wish to retract what they said, then upon them is freeing a slave or a bondmaid before they (the couple) mix with each other. From this you are given admonition, and Allah has full knowledge of all your deeds. In this verse it is stated that if after zihar there is intention of return, then first free a slave, i.e., pay kaffarah of zihar, then intercourse and its related matters become halal. The author of Hidayah says that in the Jahiliyyah, zihar was counted as divorce, meaning the marriage bond was dissolved and prohibition became permanent. Islam kept its original form but changed its ruling. Thus it said that zihar does not dissolve the marriage, but it becomes forbidden to approach the wife until kaffarah. And the prohibition due to zihar is because zihar is a crime, and it is a crime because it is an abominable and false statement, as Allah the Exalted says: 'And indeed they say an abominable statement and falsehood.' (So there is sin). (Thaanwi). So when zihar is an abominable and false statement, it is appropriate that the person be punished by making his wife forbidden to him until he pays kaffarah, and that crime is removed by kaffarah, as Allah the Exalted says: 'Indeed good deeds remove evil deeds.' And the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Follow up a bad deed with a good deed, it erases it.' That is, after evil, doing good erases the evil. So when the crime is removed by kaffarah, the prohibition also ends. Then when intercourse is forbidden due to zihar, then all things that are precursors to intercourse become forbidden, such as touching the wife, kissing her, so that these things do not lead him into intercourse. Similarly, in the state of ihram, both intercourse and its precursors are forbidden. In contrast, for the menstruating woman and the fasting person, only intercourse is forbidden, not its precursors. The reason is that menstruation and fasting occur frequently. If kissing etc. were forbidden, it would lead to hardship. As for zihar and ihram, their occurrence is rare and infrequent. Therefore, in the state of zihar and ihram, the precursors of intercourse are also forbidden, while in menstruation and fasting, the precursors are not forbidden.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage expands on the ruling of zihar. It begins by restating the central ruling: when a man says to his wife 'You are to me like my mother's back,' she becomes haram for intercourse, touching, and kissing until he pays the kaffarah. The proof is the Quranic verse from Surah al-Mujadilah (58:3-4). The text then contrasts the Islamic ruling with the pre-Islamic practice where zihar was a form of permanent divorce. Islam retained the form but changed the legal effect to a temporary prohibition linked to expiation. The reasoning is that zihar is a sinful, false statement, so punishment (prohibition) is appropriate, and its removal is through kaffarah (good deeds erase bad). The text then explains that since intercourse is forbidden, its precursors (touching, kissing) are also forbidden to prevent falling into the prohibited act, analogous to the state of ihram. This is contrasted with the cases of a menstruating woman or a fasting person, where only intercourse is forbidden, not touching or kissing. The difference lies in frequency: menstruation and fasting occur often, so forbidding precursors would cause hardship; zihar and ihram are rare, so the stricter prohibition applies.

Key Terms
ظہار (zihar): Likening one's wife to a mahram relative, making her temporarily forbidden until kaffarah.
کفارہ (kaffarah): Expiation: freeing a slave, fasting two months, or feeding sixty poor.
تماس (tamass): Touching; in zihar context, it includes intercourse and its precursors.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, why are precursors of intercourse (touching, kissing) forbidden during zihar but not during menstruation?
A) Because it is a punishment for the man
B) Because zihar and ihram occur rarely, while menstruation and fasting occur frequently, so forbidding precursors would cause hardship
C) Because the wife dislikes it
D) Because the Quran specifically mentions them

Key Takeaway
Zihar temporarily forbids all intimacy until kaffarah, with the Quranic proof and analogy to ihram emphasizing the strictness due to rarity.

Intercourse Before Expiation in Zihar: Only Istighfar Required
Ruling with proof from hadith on intercourse before kaffarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on intercourse before expiation in zihar, cite the hadith evidence, and explain why only one expiation is required.

Core Idea
Only one expiation plus istighfar; no additional kaffarah for intercourse before expiation in zihar.

When a husband declares zihar, he must complete the expiation before resuming marital relations. But what if he has intercourse before expiating? This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling, which is based on a specific hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) commanded only istighfar and did not impose an extra expiation. The lesson also contrasts the Hanafi position with minority views.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is sexual intercourse (wat') with the wife before completing the kaffarah for zihar. The Hanafi ruling: haram (forbidden) and requires istighfar; no additional kaffarah beyond the original one.
2
Locate the dalil
The ruling is based on the hadith of Salamah ibn Sakhr al-Bayadi, where the Prophet (peace be upon him) told him: 'استغفر ربك ولا تعد حتى تكفر' (Seek forgiveness from your Lord and do not repeat until you expiate).
Also narrated by Ibn Abbas and recorded by the compilers of the Sunan.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's command contains only istighfar and a prohibition on repetition until expiation. No additional kaffarah is mentioned. The Hanafi principle is that if an obligation existed, the Prophet would have clarified it. His silence indicates non-obligation.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The majority of jurists (including Abu Hanifa, Malik, Shafi'i, Ahmad) agree with one kaffarah. Amr ibn al-As held that two kaffarah are required, and Hasan al-Basri and some others held three.
The passage does not provide proofs for the opposing views.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi and relied upon by the majority. The Prophet's clear instruction indicates that only one expiation is due, and any extra obligation would have been stated.
This ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah.

کفارہ سے پہلے وطی کر لی استغفار کرے اور کچھ لازم نہیں ہے
فان وطيها قبل ان يكفر استغفر الله تعالى ولا شئ عليه غير الكفارة الاولى ولا يعاود حتى يكفر لقوله عليه السلام للذى واقع فى ظهاره قبل الكفارة استغفر الله ولا تعد حتى تكفر ولو كان شي آخر واجبا لبيئه عليه السلام قال وهذا اللفظ لا يكون الاظهارا لانه صريح فيه ولونوى به الطلاق لا يصح لانه منسوخ فلا يتمكن من الاتيان به
ترجمہ پھر اگر کفارہ دینے سے پہلے بیوی سے وطی کرلے تو اللہ تعالیٰ سے استغفار کرے اور سوائے پہلے کفارہ کے اس پر کوئی چیز واجب نہ ہوگی اور ولی کا اعادہ نہ کرے جب تک کفارہ نہ دے کیونکہ جس شخص نے ظہار میں کفارہ سے پہلے ولی کر لی تھی اس کو آنحضرت صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے یہ حکم دیا کہ اللہ تعالیٰ سے استغفار کرو اور ایسا نہ کرنا یہاں تک کہ کفارہ ویڈے اور اگر کوئی دوسری چیز واجب ہوتی تو آنحضرت اس کو ضرور بیان فرماتے ۔ مصنف نے فرمایا کہ یہ لفظ صرف ظہار ہوگا کیونکہ یہ ظہار کے معنی میں صریح ہے اور اگر اس نے اس لفظ سے
طلاق کی نیت کی تو صحیح نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس کا طلاق ہو نا منسوخ ہے تو اس کو ایسا کرنے کا اختیار نہ ہوگا۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر مظاہر نے کفارہ دینے سے پہلے اس عورت سے ولی کر لی تو یہ شخص استغفار کرے اور اس پر کفارہ اولی کے علاوہ ایک اور کفارہ واجب نہیں ہوگا اور اب وطی نہ کرے یہاں تک کہ کفارہ دیدے۔ یہی قول جمہور فقہا اور امام مالک، امام شافعی ، اور امام احمد کا ہے اور عمرو بن العاص فرماتے ہیں کہ دو کفارے واجب ہوں گے اور حسن بصری اور امام مخفی فرماتے ہیں کہ تین کفارے واجب ہوں گے ۔
ہماری دلیل یہ روایت ہے:
ان سلمة بن صخر البياضى قال الرسول الله ظاهرت من امرأتى ثم ابصرت خلخا لها في ليلة قمراء فواقعتها فقال رسول الله استغفر ربك ولا تعد حتى تكفر یعنی سلمہ بن صحر بیاضی نے حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم سے کہا کہ میں نے اپنی بیوی سے ظہار کیا پھر چاندنی رات میں ، میں نے اس کے پازیب کو دیکھا تو اس سے جماع کر بیٹھا۔ پس حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا کہ اپنے رب سے استغفار کر اور یہ حرکت دوبارہ نہ کرنا یہاں تک کہ کفارہ دیدے۔ اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ حضور نے صرف استغفار کا حکم فرمایا اور استغفار کے علاوہ اگر کوئی دوسری چیز واجب ہوتی تو آنحضرت اس کو ضرور بیان فرماتے یہ حدیث ابن عباس سے ان الفاظ کے ساتھ مروی ہے۔
ان رجلاً ظاهر من امرأته فوقع عليها قبل ان يكفر فقال له رسول الله ما حملك على هذا قال رأيت خلخا لها في ضوء القمر رواه اصحاب السنن الاربعة
اور ابن ماجہ کے الفاظ یہ ہیں:
فضحک رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم و امره ان لا يقربها حتى يكفر
فرماتے ہیں کہ اس کے قول انت علی کظهر امی سے صرف ظہار ثابت ہوگا کیونکہ ظہار کے معنی میں یہ کلام صریح ہے اور صریح

اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد پنجم محتاج نیت نہیں ہوتا چنانچہ اگر اس شخص نے انت علی کظهر امی سے طلاق کی نیت کی ۔ تو صحیح نہیں ہوگی۔۔ اس لئے کہ اس لفظ کا طلاق ہونا منسوخ ہو گیا ہے لہذا اس کو اس لفظ سے طلاق کی نیت کرنے کا اختیار نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ طلاق کی نسبت کرنے میں موضوع شرع کو متغیر کرنا لازم آتا ہے اور بندے کو اس کی اجازت نہیں ہے۔
Then if he has intercourse with her before he expiates, he seeks forgiveness from Allah Almighty, and nothing is obligatory upon him other than the first expiation, and he should not return (to intercourse) until he expiates, because of his saying (peace be upon him) to the one who had intercourse in his zihar before expiation: 'Seek forgiveness from Allah and do not return until you expiate.' And if something else were obligatory, the Prophet would have explained it. He said: And this word is only for zihar because it is explicit in it, and if he intends divorce by it, it is not valid because it is abrogated, so he is not able to do that.

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on a specific scenario in zihar: if a husband who has declared zihar has sexual intercourse with his wife before completing the required expiation. The ruling states that he must seek forgiveness (istighfar) and is not required to pay an additional expiation beyond the one already due. The primary evidence is the hadith of Salamah ibn Sakhr al-Bayadi, where the Prophet (peace be upon him) instructed him to seek forgiveness and not repeat the act until expiation is done. The commentary emphasizes that if an additional expiation were required, the Prophet would have mentioned it. The passage also clarifies that the phrase 'you are to me like my mother's back' is explicit for zihar and cannot be used for divorce, as the use of such wording for divorce has been abrogated. The text then records a disagreement: the majority of jurists (including Abu Hanifa, Malik, Shafi'i, Ahmad) hold that only one expiation is due, while Amr ibn al-As says two, and Hasan al-Basri and some others say three. The Hanafi proof is the hadith and the principle that the Prophet's silence on an additional obligation indicates its non-existence.

Key Terms
ظهار (zihar): A husband saying to his wife 'you are to me like my mother's back' or similar, which makes her forbidden until expiation.
کفارہ (kaffarah): The expiation required in zihar: freeing a slave, fasting two consecutive months, or feeding sixty poor.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on intercourse before expiation in zihar is that only one expiation is required, plus istighfar, based on the Prophet's clear instruction.

The Wording of Zihar: Explicit and Abrogated for Divorce
Definition and ruling on the explicit wording of zihar and its abrogation for divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the phrase 'you are to me like my mother's back' is explicit (sarih) for zihar and cannot be used for divorce due to abrogation (naskh).

Core Idea
Zihar wording is sarih for zihar and cannot effect divorce because it is abrogated.

In the previous lesson, we examined the ruling on intercourse before expiation. The passage continues with an important linguistic point: the phrase 'ant 'alayya ka-zahri ummi' (you are to me like my mother's back) is explicit (sarih) for zihar and does not require intention. Moreover, if someone intends divorce by these words, it is not valid because using such wording for divorce has been abrogated (mansukh). This lesson clarifies the legal implications of the wording.

Guided Path
1
Identify the phrase and its legal classification
The phrase 'ant 'alayya ka-zahri ummi' is classified as sarih (explicit) for zihar. This means it automatically establishes zihar without needing the husband's intention (niyyah).
This is a Hanafi principle: sarih wording in zihar does not require niyyah.
2
Understand the naskh (abrogation)
In pre-Islamic times or early Islam, such wording could be used for divorce, but that usage is abrogated. Therefore, if a husband says this phrase with the intention of divorce, it does not count as divorce.
Abrogation (naskh) removes the legal effect completely.
3
Apply the rule to a hypothetical
Scenario: A husband says to his wife 'ant 'alayya ka-zahri ummi' intending divorce. According to Hanafi law, the result is zihar, not divorce. The abrogation prevents the divorce from taking effect.
4
Note the legal consequence
Since it is zihar, the husband must perform expiation before resuming relations. If he intended divorce, his intention does not change the legal outcome; zihar is still established.

The primary evidence is the hadith of Salamah ibn Sakhr al-Bayadi, where the Prophet (peace be upon him) instructed him to seek forgiveness and not repeat the act until expiation is done. The commentary emphasizes that if an additional expiation were required, the Prophet would have mentioned it. The passage also clarifies that the phrase 'you are to me like my mother's back' is explicit for zihar and cannot be used for divorce, as the use of such wording for divorce has been abrogated. The text then records a disagreement: the majority of jurists (including Abu Hanifa, Malik, Shafi'i, Ahmad) hold that only one expiation is due, while Amr ibn al-As says two, and Hasan al-Basri and some others say three. The Hanafi proof is the hadith and the principle that the Prophet's silence on an additional obligation indicates its non-existence.

Key Terms
صریح (sarih): Explicit; the word 'zihar' or its derivatives are clear in meaning and do not require intention to effect zihar.
منسوخ (mansukh): Abrogated; the use of zihar wording for divorce is abrogated in Islamic law, so it cannot be used for that purpose.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling if a husband says 'ant 'alayya ka-zahri ummi' intending divorce?
A) Divorce is effective because of intention.
B) Zihar is established, not divorce.
C) Neither zihar nor divorce occurs.
D) It is considered a divorce after asking for his intention.

Key Takeaway
The zihar wording is explicit and cannot be used for divorce due to abrogation; intention does not override the explicit legal classification.
